على لسانه ما يشبه كلام الناس، فتفسد صلاته، وأما في غير الصلاة فبالعكس فلا يستظهر له دعاء لأن حفظ يمنع الرقة ،بحر، والمراد بما يشبه كلام الناس ما لا يستحيل طلبه منهم، ثم هل يشترط مع كون الدعاء مستحيلاً منهم أن يكون بلفظ وارد في الأثر المذهب لا فلو قال: اغفر لعمي، أو خالي، أو أقربائي لا تفسد خلافاً لما في الظهيرية والخلاصة، ثم التفصيل بين كونه يستحيل سؤاله من المخلوق أولاً إنما هو في - المأثور كما هو ظاهر كلام الخانية. قال في سكب الأنهر : واختار الحلبي أنّ ما هو مأثور لا يفسد مطلقاً، ويعتبر في غيره الأصل المتقدم اهـ، ومثله في الحموي عن الظهيرية قوله : ( ويفوت الواجب) وهو الخروج بلفظ السلام. قوله : (بخروجه به متعلق بقوله، ويفوت الواجب . قوله : (مثل العفو والعافية ) قال : ما سئل الله تعالى شيئاً أحب إليه من أن يسأل العافية رواه الترمذي، وجعل في الهداية لفظ الرزق مما لا يستحيل طلبه من العباد، ونظر فيه صاحب غاية البيان بأنّ إسناد الرزق إلى المخلوق مجاز لا حقيقة، والرازق الله تعالى وحده، ولذا جعله فخر الإسلام في شرحه للجامع الصغير مما يستحيل، وفصل في الخلاصة، فقال : لو قال : اللهم ارزقني فلانة الأصح الفساد ولو قال: اللهم ارزقني الحج الأصح عدمه. قال في النهر : وهذا التخريج ينبغي إعتماده ولو قال : اقض ديني تفسد
His statement: (its cause is) the mentioning of his name. His statement: (And it is recommended to supplicate for oneself, one's believing parents, and the believing men and women) due to what is related from him (peace be upon him) when he was asked: 'Which supplication is most heard?' He said: 'The depths of the last night and after the prescribed prayers.' And 'after' (dubur) is used for what is before completion, meaning the time adjacent to the time of exiting from them, and sometimes it means what is after them and their aftermath, i.e., the time following the time of exiting, and there is no impediment to intending both times, from al-Bahr. And one supplicates in Arabic, and it is forbidden to do so in a non-Arabic language because it contradicts the majesty of Allah, from al-Nahr. And it is not permissible to supplicate for forgiveness for the polytheists, and al-Qarafi declared disbelief, but the truth is otherwise due to the saying of some that the forgiveness of disbelief is rationally possible. And it is permissible to supplicate for forgiveness for all believers for all their sins due to the assumption of compassion for one's brothers, and it is a possible occurrence even if it has not happened. And it is prohibited to supplicate for customary impossibilities like the descent of a table spread, unless one is a prophet or a saint, it is said, and likewise legal impossibilities as in al-Durr. And to ask for well-being for the entire age, or the good of both worlds, and the removal of their evil, unless by it he intends specificity, for he must encounter some evil, even the agonies of death. His statement: (His statement peace be upon him etc.) The immediate understanding is that... and praise of Him, then send blessings on the Prophet, then supplicate as he wishes. However, because it is reported from him: 'This prayer of ours is not fit for any speech of men,' he placed this prohibition before the permission of supplication with what pleases him in the prayer. So he should not supplicate in it except with what resembles the words of the Quran, 'Our Lord, do not cause our hearts to deviate', and with what resembles words of the Sunnah. Among them is what is related from Abu Bakr may Allah be pleased with him that he said to the Messenger of Allah: 'Teach me, O Messenger of Allah, a supplication with which I can supplicate in my prayer.' He said: 'Say: O Allah, I have wronged myself greatly, and none forgives sins except You, so grant me forgiveness from Yourself and have mercy on me, indeed You are the Oft-Forgiving, Most Merciful.' And Ibn Mas'ud may Allah be pleased with him would supplicate with words including: 'O Allah, I ask You for all good, what I know of it and what I do not know, and I seek refuge with You from all evil, what I know of it and what I do not know.' And it is not permissible for one to supplicate in his prayer with what resembles the speech of men, because it invalidates it if it occurs before the sitting and the measure of the tashahhud, and it forfeits the obligatory [act] if it occurs after that before the salam, because he exits [the prayer] with it instead of the salam. It is like his saying: 'O Allah, marry me to so-and-so, give me gold and silver and positions,' because it is not impossible to obtain from creatures. And what is impossible like such and such supplication is outside the prayer. And this is contrary to the author's intent, because his intent is that [this ruling applies] before the salam, because he mentions the salam after. His statement: (However, because it is reported etc.) is an exception to the generality understood from the statement 'as he wishes', because it indicates the permissibility of supplication even with what is not impossible to ask from creatures while it resembles the speech of men, so the prayer becomes invalid due to the hadith 'Our prayer etc.' His statement: (with what pleases him in the prayer) i.e., from among what resembles the speech of men. His statement: ('Our Lord, do not cause our hearts to deviate') is a substitute for the words of the Quran, and he does not intend Quran but supplication, otherwise it is disliked. His statement: (And it is not permissible to supplicate etc.) Therefore they said: In prayer, one should supplicate with a memorized supplication except what occurs to him, because perhaps what resembles the speech of men might flow on his tongue, and his prayer would become invalid. But outside of prayer, it is the opposite, so he should not have a ready supplication because memorization prevents tenderness, from al-Bahr. And what is meant by 'what resembles the speech of men' is that which is not impossible to ask from them. Then, is it a condition, along with the supplication being impossible from them, that it be phrased in transmitted words? The madhhab says no. For if he says: 'Forgive my uncle, or my maternal uncle, or my relatives,' it does not invalidate, contrary to what is in al-Zahiriyya and al-Khulasa. Then the detail between whether it is impossible to ask from creatures or not is only regarding transmitted supplications, as is apparent from the words of al-Khaniyya. In Sakan al-Anhur: al-Halabi chose that what is transmitted does not invalidate absolutely, and for other [supplications] the earlier principle is considered. And similarly in al-Hamawi from al-Zahiriyya. His statement: (And it forfeits the obligatory) which is exiting with the word 'salam'. His statement: (by his exiting with it) is related to his statement 'it forfeits the obligatory'. His statement: (like pardon and well-being) He said: 'Nothing is more beloved to Allah than to ask Him for well-being' narrated by al-Tirmidhi. In al-Hidaya, the word 'rizq' is considered as not impossible to ask from creatures, but the author of Ghayat al-Bayan objected that attributing rizq to creation is metaphorical, not literal, and the sole Provider is Allah. Therefore, Fakhr al-Islam in his commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir considered it impossible. In al-Khulasa, he detailed: if he says 'O Allah, provide me with so-and-so,' the correct view is invalidation; if he says 'O Allah, provide me with Hajj,' the correct view is no invalidation. In al-Nahr: This distinction should be adopted. If he says 'pay my debt,' it invalidates.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage is a detailed hashiah commentary on the rulings regarding du'a (supplication) in prayer. The author, al-Tahtawi, is explaining the conditions and limitations of du'a within the salah. The base matn likely said 'and it is recommended to supplicate for oneself...' but the hashiah expands significantly. The passage covers several key points: (1) The recommended times for du'a: the last part of the night and after the prescribed prayers. There is a discussion about the meaning of 'dubur' (after) – whether it is before or after the prayer. (2) Du'a should be in Arabic; using other languages is forbidden because it contradicts the majesty of Allah. (3) It is not permissible to supplicate for forgiveness for polytheists, though the commentator notes some rational debate. (4) One may supplicate for all believers for all sins due to compassion. (5) It is prohibited to ask for things that are impossible by custom, like the descent of a heavenly table, unless the person is a prophet or saint. (6) Asking for well-being for the entire age or good of both worlds is allowed, but one must inevitably encounter some evil (like death pangs). The main focus shifts to the ruling on du'a in prayer. The hadith 'Our prayer is not fit for any speech of men' is used to restrict du'a in prayer: one must not use phrases that resemble the ordinary speech of people (kalam al-nas). Such speech invalidates the prayer if it occurs before the sitting for tashahhud; if after, it causes one to miss the obligatory salam. Examples given: asking for marriage or money are considered 'speech of men' because such things can be requested from humans. The passage then discusses the details: The relied upon position is that the du'a must generally resemble Quranic and Sunnah wording. However, there is a detail regarding transmitted du'as (ma'thur) vs. non-transmitted. Al-Halabi opined that ma'thur du'a never invalidates, while for non-ma'thur, the principle of resemblance to speech of men applies. A distinction is also made about whether the thing asked for is possible from creatures (like rizq from a person) or impossible (like rizq from only Allah). The text notes that asking for rizq from a specific woman is considered invalidating, but asking for Hajj is not. The passage ends with a ruling on asking for debt repayment. The overall message is that du'a in prayer must avoid any phrasing that could be mistaken for conversational speech, and should be in the spirit of worship, not mundane transactions.

Key Terms
الدعاء (al-du'a): Supplication, i.e., asking Allah for something. In this context, it is a recommended act in prayer but subject to conditions.
كلام الناس (kalam al-nas): The ordinary speech of people, which is not allowed in prayer. This includes asking for worldly favors that one might ask from another human.
المأثور (al-ma'thur): Supplications that are transmitted from the Prophet (peace be upon him) or the righteous predecessors, as opposed to invented ones.
يُفَوِّتُ الْوَاجِبَ (yufawwit al-wajib): Forfeits the obligatory act. In this context, if prohibited du'a occurs after tashahhud, the obligatory salam is lost, meaning the prayer is valid but the salat is incomplete; the person has not exited properly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a worshipper says after tashahhud: 'O Allah, provide me with a good wife and a large house'?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but the obligatory salam is forfeited.
C) The prayer is valid and no penalty because du'a is always allowed.
D) The prayer is valid only if said in Arabic.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, du'a in prayer must avoid any phrase that could be a request from a human; violating this before tashahhud invalidates the prayer, while after tashahhud it forfeits the obligatory salam.

Salah — Prayer

When Du'a Invalidates Salah
Critical refinement of du'a rules in salah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish permissible from invalidating du'a in salah according to the Hanafi school and apply the relied-upon distinction from al-Khulasa.

Core Idea
If a du'a resembles a request possible from humans, it invalidates salah; asking for what only Allah gives is fine.

Supplication (du'a) is a beautiful act in salah, but it is not unrestricted. The Prophet ﷺ said, 'This prayer of ours is not suitable for any of the speech of people.' This lesson explores which du'as are permitted and which cross the line into 'kalam al-nas', potentially invalidating your prayer. We will analyze the primary proof, the examples from the Sunnah, and an important intra-Hanafi dispute about asking for worldly provision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
Du'a in salah is generally permissible (mubah) after tashahhud, but the Prophet's hadith restricts it to words resembling Quran and Sunnah.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the hadith 'إن صلاتنا هذه لا يصلح فيها شيء من كلام الناس' and understand its implication: any speech that could be addressed to a human is prohibited and invalidates if done before tashahhud.
Hadith is authentic (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalala).
3
Apply the dalil to distinguish du'as
Examine examples: du'as from Quran and Sunnah (e.g., Rabbana la tuzigh qulubana) are allowed; asking for marriage to a specific person or worldly goods (gold, positions) is not.
Key test: can this request be obtained from human beings? If yes, it is kalam al-nas.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on 'rizq'
Scholars differed on asking for 'rizq'. Al-Hidayah said it is not impossible; Ghayat al-Bayan and Fakhr al-Islam considered it impossible (since only Allah provides). Al-Khulasa distinguished: asking for a specific person invalidates, asking for Hajj does not.
The distinction is based on whether the request is typically sought from people (like a spouse) or purely from Allah (like Hajj).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later authorities like al-Nahr prefer the distinction in al-Khulasa. This is the operative ruling: asking for a specific person or direct human grant invalidates; asking for spiritual or impossible-for-humans matters does not.
This is the relied-upon position for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثناء عليه ثم ليصل على النبي ثم ليدع بعد ما شاء لكن لما ورد عنه : إن صلاتنا هذه لا يصلح فيها شيء من كلام الناس قدم هذا المانع على إباحة الدعاء بما أعجبه في الصلاة فلا يدعو فيها إلا بما يشبه ألفاظ القرآن ربنا لا تزع قلوبنا (و) بما يشبه ألفاظ (السنة) ومنها ما روي عن أبي بكر رضي الله تعالى عنه أنه قال لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : علمني يا رسول الله دعاء أدعو به في صلاتي فقال: قل اللهم إني ظلمت نفسي ظلماً كثيراً وإنه لا يغفر الذنوب إلا أنت فاغفر لي مغفرة من عندك وارحمني إنك أنت الغفور الرحيم، وكان ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه يدعو بكلمات منها اللهم إني أسألك من الخير كله ما علمت منه وما لم أعلم وأعوذ بك من الشر كله ما علمت منه وما لم أعلم و(لا) يجوز أن يدعو في صلاته بما يشبه كلام الناس لأنه يبطلها إن وجد قبل القعود وقدر التشهد ويفوت الواجب لوجوده بعده قبل السلام بخروجه به دون السلام، وهو مثل قوله اللهم زوجني فلانة أعطني من الذهب والفضة والمناصب لأنه لا يستحيل حصوله من العباد، وما يستحيل مثل العفو والعافية قال : ما سئل الله تعالى شيئاً أحب إليه من أن يسأل العافية رواه الترمذي، وجعل في الهداية لفظ الرزق مما لا يستحيل طلبه من العباد، ونظر فيه صاحب غاية البيان بأنّ إسناد الرزق إلى المخلوق مجاز لا حقيقة، والرازق الله تعالى وحده، ولذا جعله فخر الإسلام في شرحه للجامع الصغير مما يستحيل، وفصل في الخلاصة، فقال : لو قال : اللهم ارزقني فلانة الأصح الفساد ولو قال: اللهم ارزقني الحج الأصح عدمه. قال في النهر : وهذا التخريج ينبغي إعتماده ولو قال : اقض ديني تفسد
And praising Him, then sending blessings upon the Prophet, then supplicating as he wishes, but because it has been reported from him (peace be upon him): 'This prayer of ours is not suitable for any of the speech of people,' this prevention was given precedence over the permissibility of supplication with whatever he likes in prayer. So he should not supplicate in it except with what resembles the words of the Qur'an — 'Our Lord, do not cause our hearts to deviate' — and with what resembles the words of the Sunnah. Among them is what is narrated from Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'Teach me, O Messenger of Allah, a supplication with which I may supplicate in my prayer.' He said: 'Say: O Allah, I have wronged myself greatly, and no one forgives sins except You, so grant me forgiveness from Yourself and have mercy on me; indeed, You are the Oft-Forgiving, the Most Merciful.' And Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) used to supplicate with words including: 'O Allah, I ask You for all that is good, what I know and what I do not know, and I seek refuge in You from all that is evil, what I know and what I do not know.' And it is not permissible to supplicate in prayer with what resembles the speech of people, because it invalidates it if it occurs before the sitting (qa'dah) and the amount of tashahhud, and it causes the obligatory act to be missed if it occurs after that before the salaam, due to exiting with it instead of the salaam. An example is saying: 'O Allah, marry me to so-and-so, give me gold, silver, and positions,' because it is not impossible to obtain from people. And what is impossible is like forgiveness and well-being. He said: Nothing is asked of Allah that is more beloved to Him than asking for well-being; narrated by Tirmidhi. And in al-Hidayah, the word 'rizq' is considered among that which is not impossible to ask from people. The author of Ghayat al-Bayan objected that attributing rizq to a creature is metaphorical, not real, and Allah alone is the Provider. Therefore, Fakhr al-Islam in his commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir considered it impossible. And a distinction was made in al-Khulasa: if one says 'O Allah, provide me with so-and-so', the correct view is that it invalidates; if one says 'O Allah, provide me with Hajj', the correct view is that it does not invalidate. In al-Nahr, it is said: This distinction should be relied upon. And if he says 'Pay my debt', it invalidates.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) on the rules of supplication (du'a) during salah. The author, Al-Tahtawi, comments on the matn of Maraqi al-Falah. The central ruling is that while du'a is permissible in salah, it is restricted to words that resemble the Quran and Sunnah. The reason is the prophetic hadith: 'This prayer of ours is not suitable for any of the speech of people.' Therefore, if one uses words that could be addressed to a human being, such as asking for marriage or wealth, it invalidates the prayer. However, if the request is impossible for a human to grant (like forgiveness or well-being), it is permissible. The text provides examples from the Sunnah, such as the du'a taught to Abu Bakr and the du'a of Ibn Mas'ud. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether asking for 'rizq' (provision) invalidates. Al-Hidayah considers 'rizq' as not impossible to ask from people, but others argue that only Allah provides, so it is impossible. The distinction in al-Khulasa: asking for a specific person invalidates, but asking for Hajj does not. This distinction is preferred by later authorities.

Key Terms
الدعاء (al-du'a): Supplication in salah; can be any words addressed to Allah, but restricted to what resembles Quran and Sunnah to avoid invalidating the prayer.
كلام الناس (kalam al-nas): Speech of people; any words that could be used in ordinary conversation or requests among humans. Using such words in salah invalidates it.
الواجب (al-wajib): The obligatory act (here: the final salaam). If du'a like human speech occurs after tashahhud, it causes the wajib to be missed if the person then exits without the salaam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following supplications would INVALIDATE the salah according to the preferred Hanafi position in this passage?
A) اللهم ارزقني الحج
B) اللهم ارزقني فلانة
C) ربنا لا تزع قلوبنا
D) اللهم إني ظلمت نفسي

Key Takeaway
Supplication in salah must avoid words that could be addressed to humans; asking for what only Allah gives (e.g., Hajj) is allowed, but asking for worldly goods that humans can grant invalidates.

Sunnahs of Taslim and Niyyah of Imam
Critical refinement of taslim and niyyah sunnahs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah actions of taslim, explain the dispute regarding adding 'wa barakatuh', and identify the sunnah for the imam's intention in prayer.

Core Idea
Taslim's sunnah actions are turning and standard wording; adding 'wa barakatuh' is established by hadith and not bid'ah.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi refines two important sunnahs in prayer: the physical and verbal details of the closing taslim, and the scope of the imam's intention. You will learn the precise sunnah actions, the evidence for adding 'wa barakatuh', and whom the imam should intend to include in his prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnahs of taslim
Determine from the passage what physical actions and wordings are considered sunnah in taslim. Note that turning the head and saying the full greeting are sunnah, while omitting them does not invalidate the prayer.
The matn states it is sunnah to turn to the right and left with two greetings.
2
Analyze the dispute on adding 'wa barakatuh'
The author refutes the claim that adding 'wa barakatuh' is an innovation. Follow the evidence presented: the hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud, and the citation of al-Halabi from Mukhtalaf al-Fatawa.
The hadith shows the Prophet saying 'wa barakatuh' on the right.
3
Understand the ruling on imam's niyyah
The passage states it is sunnah for the imam to intend men, women, boys, hermaphrodites, and the guardian angels. Note that specifying numbers for angels is not required due to differences.
This is a refinement: the imam should include all groups present.
4
Examine the details about hafazah
The commentary elaborates on the guardian angels: their function, number, and what they write. While not directly fiqh, this contextualizes the niyyah ruling.
The correct view is that deeds of disbelievers and discerning children are also recorded.

المسجد والأصح ما لم يستدر القبلة كما في الدر. قوله : (والنساء) وهذا أولى مما في النهر أنه لا ينويهن إن حضرن لكراهة حضورهن لأن الكراهة عليهن، وهذا مطلوب منه إذا صلين معه فالجهة منفكة . قوله : الحفظهم ما يصدر من الإنسان من قول، وعمل) فعن يمينه رقيب، وهو كاتب الحسنات، وعن يساره عتيد، وهو كاتب السيآت وورد أنه إذا مات ابن آدم يأمرهما الله تعالى بالإقامة على قبره يحمدانه ويسبحانه، ويهللانه، ويكبرانه، ويكتب ذلك لصاحبهما حتى يبعث، ويفارقانه عند الغائط والجماع، والأصح أن الكافر تكتب أعماله، وأن الصبي المميز تكتب حسناته، وكيفية الكتابة والمكتوب فيه مما استأثر الله بعلمه على الأصح، واختلف في محل الجلوس، فقيل : الفم والمداد الريق، والقلم اللسان الخبر نقوا أفواهكم بالخلال فإنها مجلس الملائكة الحافظين، وقيل: على اليمين والشمال واختلف فيما يكتبانه قيل ما فيه أجر، ووزر لما ورد أن كاتب الحسنات أمين على كاتب السيآت فإذا عمل حسنة كتبها عشرا وإن عمل سيئة قال له : دعه ساعات لعله يسبح، أو يستغفر، وفي بعض الكتب ست ساعات، وقيل: يكتبان كل شيء واختلف في وقت محو المباح، والأكثر على أنه يوم القيامة. قوله : (أو) لحفظهم إياه من الجن وأسباب المعاطب) أي المهالك، وكذا سبع
And it is Sunnah to turn to the right, then to the left with two greetings, because he (peace be upon him) used to salute from his right saying 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah' until the whiteness of his right cheek was seen, and from his left 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah' until the whiteness of his left cheek was seen. If he reduces and says 'Assalamu alaykum' or 'Salamu alaykum', he abandons the Sunnah, but the obligatory part is valid. He should not add 'wa barakatuh' because it is an innovation and nothing is established about it. If he begins with the left, forgetfully or intentionally, he salutes from his right and does not repeat it on his left, and there is nothing upon him except the offense of intention. If he salutes directly in front of him, he salutes from his left. If he forgets his left and stands up, he returns as long as he has not left the mosque or spoken; then he sits and salutes. And it is Sunnah for the imam to intend men, women, boys, hermaphrodites, and the angels (the hafazah) – plural of hafiz, so called for preserving what comes from a person of speech and action, or for preserving him from jinn and causes of destruction. He does not specify a number due to differences. Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) said: With every believer are five of the hafazah, one on his right writes... in hidden things. And it is objected that in the Sunnah it is reported 'Pay our debt for us and enrich us from poverty' – but it may be said that the meaning of 'athar' (tradition) regarding du'a after tashahhud is that it should be transmitted for prayer specifically, not absolutely; this is farfetched. So in al-Bahr. His statement: (with two greetings) is on the basis of distribution. His statement: 'until the whiteness of his cheek is seen' is passive voice in both places. His statement: 'said Assalamu alaykum or Alaykum assalam' His statement: 'because it is an innovation' – said by Nawawi, but it is refuted by what came in Sunan Abi Dawud from Alqamah ibn Wa'il from his father: I prayed with the Prophet and he used to salute from his right 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah wa barakatuh' and from his left 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah'. And it was stopped upon him. Then al-Mundhiri and in al-Halabi from Mukhtalaf al-Fatawa that he added 'wa barakatuh' in both greetings. His statement: (as long as he has not left the mosque – the correct view is as long as he has not turned away from the qiblah, as in al-Durr. His statement: (and women) – this is better than what is in al-Nahr that he does not intend them if they are present due to dislike of their presence, because the dislike is upon them, and this is required of him if they pray with him, so the direction is separate. His statement: 'preservation of what comes from a person of speech and action' – on his right is a watcher, who writes good deeds, and on his left is a recorder, who writes evil deeds. It is reported that when the son of Adam dies, Allah commands them to stay at his grave, praising, glorifying, declaring His oneness, and magnifying Him, and that is written for their companion until he is resurrected. And they leave him at the time of relieving oneself and intercourse. The correct view is that the disbeliever's deeds are written, and the discerning child's good deeds are written. The manner of writing and the material on which it is written are among the things Allah has kept knowledge of to Himself, according to the correct view. They differed regarding the place of sitting: it is said the mouth and the ink is saliva, and the pen is the tongue – the hadith: 'Clean your mouths with toothpicks for they are the seat of the guardian angels.' And it is said: on the right and left. They differed as to what they write: it is said only what has reward and burden, because of the report that the writer of good deeds is an overseer over the writer of evil deeds. When he does a good deed, he writes it ten times, and when he does an evil deed, he says to him: 'Wait for hours, perhaps he will glorify or seek forgiveness' – in some books, six hours. And it is said they write everything. They differed about the time of erasing permissible acts, and the majority view is that it is on the Day of Judgment. His statement: (or) for preserving him from jinn and causes of destruction – i.e., disasters, and likewise seven.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) on the rulings of taslim (greeting of peace) and the intention of the imam when leading prayer. The matn states that it is Sunnah to turn the face to the right and left while saying the taslim. The commentator clarifies details: if one reduces the wording, the Sunnah is omitted but the prayer is valid; adding 'wa barakatuh' is considered an innovation by some, but there is evidence from Sunan Abi Dawud that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did say it. The commentator prefers the view that it is permissible to add 'wa barakatuh' based on that hadith. The second part discusses the intention of the imam: he should intend men, women, boys, hermaphrodites, and the guardian angels (hafazah). The term 'hafazah' is explained in detail: they are angels that record deeds and protect from jinn and harm. Various opinions about their number, function, and writing are discussed, such as the report from Ibn Abbas that there are five per believer. The commentator also addresses an objection about a du'a for debt payment, which seems to be a carryover from the previous discussion, but it is refuted with the explanation that the transmitted du'a is specifically for after tashahhud.

Key Terms
التسليم (al-taslim): The greeting of peace at the end of prayer, consisting of saying 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah' while turning the head right then left.
الحفظة (al-hafazah): Guardian angels that record deeds and protect humans; also called Kiraman Katibin. The imam intends them in his niyyah for the prayer.
النية (al-niyyah): Intention of the imam for those he leads, including men, women, etc. and the angels.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on an imam who turns only to the right and says 'Assalamu alaykum'?
A) His prayer is void because he omitted a fard.
B) His prayer is valid but he has omitted a sunnah.
C) He must repeat the prayer.
D) His prayer is incomplete and must be made up later.

Key Takeaway
The sunnahs of taslim include turning and the full greeting; adding 'wa barakatuh' is permissible based on hadith, and the imam's niyyah should include all present including guardian angels.

Imam's Intention for Unseen Beings in Congregation
Ruling on imam's intention for unseen participants in salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state whom the imam should intend when making the final salam and identify the relied-upon view regarding the number of salams.

Core Idea
The imam's intention extends to angels and righteous jinn, not only visible worshippers.

When the imam says the final salam in congregational prayer, he is not only greeting the visible worshippers. Classical Hanafi texts explain that he should also intend the recording angels and the righteous jinn who follow him. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the preferred practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the imam's intention (niyyah) for the concluding salam. The ruling is that it is sunnah (recommended) to intend specific groups.
Intention here refers to a heartfelt awareness, not verbal utterance.
2
List the groups to be intended
The text lists: men, women, children, hermaphrodites, the recording angels (al-hafazah), and the righteous jinn (salih al-jinn) who follow the imam in prayer.
Hermaphrodites (al-khunatha) are included as a distinct category.
3
Understand the belief about angels
The text provides details about the recording angels: there are various reports about their number (5, 60, 160) but no definitive count. Belief in them is obligatory without specifying numbers.
The angels are present with every believer.
4
Examine the ikhtilaf on salams for jinn
There is a difference of opinion: the relied-upon (al-ashah) view is that the imam intends all, including jinn, with both salams. Some say only the first salam, others say the gesture of turning suffices.
The text uses 'قيل' for the weaker opinions.
5
State the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is to intend all groups with both salams, as stated by Al-Tahtawi.
This is the strongest position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يسن (نية الإمام الرجال والنساء والصبيان والخنائي (و) الملائكة (الحفظة) جمع حافظ سموا به لحفظهم ما يصدر من الإنسان من قول وعمل أو لحفظهم إياه من الجن وأسباب المعاطب، ولا يعين عدداً للأختلاف فيه، وعن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما أنه قال : مع كل مؤمن خمس من الحفظة واحد عن يمينه يكتب الحسنات وواحد عن يساره يكتب السيآت وآخر أمامه يلقنه الخيرات وآخر وراءه يدفع عنه المكاره، وآخره عند ناصيته يكتب ما يصلي على النبي ويبلغه إلى الرسول عليه السلام وقيل معه ستون ملكاً وقيل مائة وستون يذبون عنه الشياطين فالإيمان بهم كالإيمان بالأنبياء عليهم السلام من غير حصر بعدد (و) نيته (صالح الجن) المقتدين به فينوي الإمام الجميع (بالتسليمتين في الأصح لأنه يخاطبهم وقيل : ينويهم بالتسليمة الأولى وقيل تكفيه الإشارة إليهم
And it is sunnah for the imam to intend with his salam: the men, women, children, and hermaphrodites, and the recording angels (al-hafazah), plural of hafiz, so called because they preserve what issues from a person of speech and action, or preserve him from jinn and causes of destruction. He does not specify a number due to difference of opinion. It is narrated from Ibn Abbas that with every believer there are five recording angels: one on his right writes good deeds, one on his left writes evil deeds, one in front teaches him good, one behind repels calamities, and one at his forelock writes what he sends blessings on the Prophet and conveys it to the Messenger. And it is said that with him are sixty angels, or one hundred and sixty, who repel the devils. Belief in them is like belief in the prophets, without specifying a number. And also the righteous jinn who follow him (the imam), so the imam intends all of them with the two salams according to the more correct view, because he addresses them. It is also said he intends them with the first salam, and it is said that the gesture (turning) suffices for them.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the imam's niyyah (intention) for the concluding salam. It is sunnah for the imam to intend, in his heart, all those who are present in the congregation: men, women, children, and hermaphrodites. Additionally, he should intend the recording angels (al-hafazah) and the righteous jinn who are following him in prayer. The text discusses the belief in the angels, stating that there is no definitive number, and reports various traditions: from Ibn Abbas that there are five angels per believer, others sixty or one hundred and sixty. The key point is that belief in them is obligatory in general, without specifying a number. Regarding the jinn, only those following the imam in prayer are intended. There is a difference of opinion: the most correct view is that the imam intends them with both salams (since he addresses them), some say only the first salam suffices, and others say the physical gesture of turning is enough. This reflects the importance of intention and the spiritual entities present in congregational prayer.

Key Terms
الحفظة (al-hafazah): The recording angels who write down a person's deeds.
صالح الجن (salih al-jinn): Righteous jinn who follow the imam in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) With both salams
B) Only the first salam
C) Only the second salam
D) The gesture of turning suffices

Key Takeaway
The imam's intention should encompass all beings present, visible and invisible, and the relied-upon view is to intend them with both salams.

Intention of the Follower and the Individual
Rulings on whom the follower and individual worshipper intend with the salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah intention for the salam for both the follower and the individual worshipper in the Hanafi school and apply the rules according to the imam's position.

Core Idea
The follower intends the imam, congregation, angels, and jinn; the individual intends only the angels.

In the Hanafi school, the salam at the end of prayer is not just words; it carries a recommended intention for specific beings. This lesson explains whom the follower (ma'mum) and the lone worshipper (munfarid) should intend when saying the salam, and how the position of the imam affects the follower's intention. Understanding this sunnah enhances the spiritual connection of the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The text distinguishes between the follower (ma'mum) and the individual (munfarid). Each has a distinct ruling for whom to intend with the salam.
The follower is praying behind an imam; the individual is alone.
2
Determine the follower's intention based on imam's location
If the imam is to the right, the follower intends him with the right salam; if to the left, with the left salam; if directly in front, with both salams.
The imam has a share from each direction when directly ahead.
3
Include additional beings for the follower
Besides the imam, the follower also intends the congregation (qawm), the recording angels (hafazah), and the righteous jinn (salih al-jinn).
This completes the sunnah intention.
4
Apply the ruling for the individual
The individual intends only the angels, because there is no congregation or imam to address.
No need to intend any other beings.
5
Understand the rationale
The imam is given special consideration because he benefits the follower by leading the prayer. The other beings are also present and deserving of greeting.
This reflects the comprehensive etiquette of the salam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يسن (نية المأموم امامه في جهته اليمين إن كان فيها، أو اليسار إن كان فيها (وإن حاذاه نواه في التسليمتين لأنّ له حظا من كل جهة وهو أحق من الحاضرين لأنه أحسن إلى المأموم بالتزام صلاته (مع القوم والحفظة وصالح الجن و يسن (نية المنفرد الملائكة فقط) غيرهم
And it is sunnah for the follower to intend his imam in his direction, on the right if the imam is there, or on the left if he is there. And if the imam is directly in front of him, then he should intend him in both salams because he has a share from every direction, and he (the imam) has more right than the other attendees because he benefitted the follower by undertaking his prayer. Along with the people, the recording angels, and the righteous jinn. And it is sunnah for the individual to intend only the angels, not others.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage addresses the niyyah for the salam of the follower (ma'mum) and the individual (munfarid). The follower should intend his imam specifically, based on where the imam is located: if to his right, he intends him with the right salam; if to his left, with the left salam; if directly in front, he intends him with both salams. This is because the imam has a special right over the follower, having led his prayer. In addition to the imam, the follower also intends the entire congregation, the angels, and the righteous jinn. The individual, however, only intends the angels, because there is no congregation to address. The commentator notes that this is a point often overlooked by scholars and laypeople alike, highlighting its importance. This ruling emphasizes the etiquette of the salam and the connection between the worshipper and the unseen beings present.

Key Terms
المأموم (al-ma'mum): The person praying behind the imam.
المنفرد (al-munfarid): The person praying alone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Both salams
B) The right salam only
C) The left salam only
D) Neither, because the imam is not in front

Key Takeaway
The follower's intention for the salam includes the imam (based on direction), congregation, angels, and jinn, while the individual intends only the angels.

Niyyah of the Imam and Munfarid in the Taslim
Explains whom the imam and munfarid intend in taslim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state whom the imam, muqtadi, and munfarid should intend in the taslim, and identify the preferred Hanafi view on the imam’s intention.

Core Idea
The Imam intends all with both taslims; the munfarid intends only the angels.

The final taslim of the prayer is not merely a physical act—it carries an intention (niyyah) that addresses beings present. This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi details whom the imam, the follower (muqtadi), and the individual praying alone (munfarid) should have in mind when saying the salams. Understanding this nuance completes the spiritual discipline of the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling category
Recognize that the act is the intention (niyyah) during the two taslims. The taslim itself is wajib, but the specific intention of whom to address is sunnah for the muqtadi and munfarid, and the most correct practice (al-ah) for the imam.
2
Determine the imam’s intention
According to the most correct view, the imam intends all present—the congregation, the guardian angels, and the righteous jinn—with both his right and left taslims, because he addresses them. Alternate views say only the first taslim suffices or that a gesture suffices.
The author supports the view that both taslims require this intention.
3
Examine the muqtadi’s intention
The follower (muqtadi) should intend his imam in his direction: if the imam is on his right, he intends him in the right taslim; if on his left, in the left; if directly in front, he intends him in both taslims.
The imam is more entitled because he undertook the prayer for the follower.
4
Examine the munfarid’s intention
The individual praying alone (munfarid) should intend only the angels (the guardian angels) in his taslims, not any congregation or jinn.
This is sunnah and often neglected, as the commentator notes.
5
Synthesize the ruling
Combine all three scenarios: the imam intends all in both taslims, the muqtadi intends the imam (accounting for direction), and the munfarid intends only the angels. All are sunnah except the imam’s intention, which is the most correct practice.
The internal Hanafi ikhtilaf about the imam is resolved by preferring the view of both taslims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) نيته (صالح الجن) المقتدين به فينوي الإمام الجميع (بالتسليمتين في الأصح لأنه يخاطبهم وقيل : ينويهم بالتسليمة الأولى وقيل تكفيه الإشارة إليهم (و) يسن (نية المأموم امامه في جهته اليمين إن كان فيها، أو اليسار إن كان فيها (وإن حاذاه نواه في التسليمتين لأنّ له حظا من كل جهة وهو أحق من الحاضرين لأنه أحسن إلى المأموم بالتزام صلاته (مع القوم والحفظة وصالح الجن و يسن (نية المنفرد الملائكة فقط) غيرهم وينبغي التنبه لهذا فإنه قل من يتنبه له من أهل العلم فضلا عن غيرهم
And his intention (for the righteous jinn) of those following him, so the Imam intends all (the congregation, angels, and righteous jinn) with the two taslims according to the most correct view because he addresses them. And it was said: he intends them with the first taslim. And it was said: the gesture to them suffices him. And it is sunnah for the muqtadi (follower) to intend his Imam in his direction, on his right if he is there, or on his left if he is there. And if he is directly in front of him, he intends him in both taslims because he has a share from every direction, and he is more entitled than those present because he has done good to the follower by undertaking his prayer. (Along with the people, the guardian angels, and the righteous jinn.) And it is sunnah for the munfarid (individual) to intend only the angels besides them. And one should pay attention to this, for few among the people of knowledge pay attention to it, let alone others.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the intention (niyyah) in the final taslim of the prayer. It clarifies whom the Imam, the muqtadi, and the munfarid should have in mind when saying the salam. The author supports the view that the Imam intends all present (congregation, angels, and righteous jinn) with both taslims, as he addresses them. An alternate view suggests the first taslim suffices, while another says a gesture suffices. The muqtadi is advised to intend the Imam according to his direction. The munfarid only intends the angels, as he has no congregation. The commentator stresses that this is often overlooked.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention in the heart; here, whom one addresses with the salam.
التسليمتان (al-taslimatayn): The two salams at the end of prayer (to the right and left).
المنفرد (al-munfarid): One praying alone, not in congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Whom should the munfarid (individual praying alone) intend in his taslim?
A) The congregation
B) The angels only
C) The Imam
D) The angels and the righteous jinn

Key Takeaway
The Imam intends all with both taslims; the muqtadi intends the imam according to direction; the munfarid intends only the angels—all are sunnah and often neglected.

Adab of Taslim and Adab of Prayer
Rulings on lowering voice in second taslim, muqtadi's taslim timing, and beginning of adab al-salat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah acts related to taslim and the general adab of prayer, and identify the ikhtilaf on muqtadi's taslim timing.

Core Idea
The second taslim should be quiet; the muqtadi's taslim timing is disputed among Hanafi imams.

This passage covers several sunnah acts related to the concluding salam and the broader etiquette of prayer. It also introduces the concept of 'adab' as actions the Prophet performed irregularly. We will examine each ruling and the minor ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school on when the follower says his salam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah acts of taslim
Read the first part of the passage and list the four rulings: lowering the second taslim, muqtadi's taslim timing, starting with the right, and the masbuq waiting for the imam.
These are all sunnah, not wajib.
2
Understand the ikhtilaf on muqtadi's taslim
Note the difference between Imam Abu Hanifa (coincide) and the two companions (after). Recognize that the relied-upon view is after.
The ikhtilaf is based on different interpretations of following the imam.
3
Review the adab of prayer
After the taslim section, the passage defines adab and gives examples: man taking hands out for takbir, woman covering hands, and the beginning of rulings on looking.
Adab are sunnah acts not done persistently.

And it is sunnah to lower his voice with the second taslim lower than the first. And it is sunnah for the muqtadi's taslim to coincide with the imam's taslim according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and after his taslim according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), so that he does not hasten to worldly matters. And it is sunnah to begin with the right side, as we have explained. And it is sunnah for the one who missed a part (masbuq) to wait for the imam to finish (his taslim) due to the obligation of following (the imam) until he knows that there is no forgetfulness (sahw) upon him. Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage covers a set of sunnah acts related to the taslim and general adab of prayer. It states that the second taslim should be quieter than the first. The muqtadi should say his taslim either simultaneously with the imam (according to Imam Abu Hanifa) or after him (according to the two companions). It is sunnah to start the salam with the right side first. The masbuq must wait for the imam to complete his taslim before he finishes his own prayer, because he must follow the imam until sure there is no forgetfulness. Then a new section on adab begins, defining adab as actions the Prophet did once or twice without continuing, such as extra tasbihat in bowing and prostration. Among the adab: for men to take their hands out of sleeves for the opening takbir, except for necessity; women cover their hands to avoid exposing forearms; and the ruling on where to look during prayer is introduced.

Key Terms
الأدب (al-adab): An action done by the Prophet once or twice without persistence; sunnah but not stressed.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): One who joined the congregation late and missed some rak'ahs.
التسليمة الثانية (al-taslimat al-thaniyah): The second salam (to the left) at the end of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Muqtadi's Salam Timing: Simultaneous or After the Imam?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on muqtadi's salam timing and associated sunan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the muqtadi's salam timing and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
The muqtadi should say salam after the imam to avoid hurrying; this is the mufta bihi view.

The final salam (taslim) contains several sunan acts. Among them is the timing of the muqtadi's salam relative to the imam – a point of intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. In this lesson, you will examine the views of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, understand their proofs, and learn which position is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunan
List the four recommended acts (sunan) mentioned in the passage related to the salam.
They include lowering voice, muqtadi's timing, starting with right, and masbuq waiting.
2
Locate the dispute
Find where the passage mentions the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on muqtadi's salam timing.
The phrase 'عند الإمام' vs 'عندهما' indicates the ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the evidence
Consider the reasoning behind each view: Abu Hanifa's muqaranah (simultaneous) and the Sahibayn's caution against hurrying.
The hadith 'the imam is appointed to be followed' supports both interpretations.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Identify which view is adopted for fatwa practice and why.
Al-Tahtawi notes 'lest he hurry with worldly matters' as the tarjih reason.
5
Apply to practice
Describe how a Hanafi muqtadi should act in a real mosque setting based on the mufta bihi view.
He should wait until the imam completes both salams, then say his own.

And it is sunnah to lower his voice in the second greeting compared to the first. And it is sunnah for the follower to accompany the imam's greeting according to Abu Hanifa, to be in correspondence with him, and after his greeting according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), lest he hurry with worldly matters. And it is sunnah to begin with the right (side), which we have explained. He said: 'And it is sunnah to lower his voice in the second greeting' — al-Halabi specified it for the imam, and al-Sayyid mentioned it, and it is in the text of Munyat al-Musalli, because the sunnah for him is to raise his voice in the dhikrs of transitions, because all are for informing others of his state. He said: 'And it is sunnah for the latecomer to wait for the imam to finish' — i.e., from his two greetings. He said: 'Due to the obligation of following' — for if he stands before him, it is makruh tahriman, and it may be permissible for him to stand out of necessity, such as if he fears that if he waits, the time of Fajr, Jumu'ah, or 'Eid would pass, or the duration of his wiping (mas-h) would elapse, or the time would exit while he is excused, and similarly if he fears people passing in front of him. And Allah Most High knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the Magnificent.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage is a hashiya commentary on the sunan related to the final greeting (salam) of prayer. It discusses several recommended acts: lowering the voice in the second salam, the follower's timing of salam, beginning with the right side, and the latecomer waiting for the imam. The key intra-Hanafi dispute is whether the muqtadi should say salam simultaneously with the imam (view of Imam Abu Hanifa) or after the imam has completed his salam (view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The commentary also clarifies that it is recommended for the imam to raise his voice in the transitional dhikrs to inform the congregation, and that the latecomer must wait for the imam to finish both salams before standing, unless a necessity arises.

Key Terms
مقارنة (muqāranah): The act of the muqtadi saying salam simultaneously with the imam.
تسليمة (taslīmah): Each of the two salams at the end of prayer (one to the right, one to the left).
مسبوق (masbūq): A latecomer who joined the prayer after the imam has already started, missing one or more rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Definition of Adab and Its Place in Prayer
Hashiya defining adab and distinguishing from mustahabb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define adab in Hanafi terminology, distinguish it from mustahabb, and apply it to specific actions in prayer.

Core Idea
Adab completes the sunnah through occasional practices that enhance khushu’.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah clarifies a subtle Hanafi category: adab. Unlike mustahabb (done regularly but without persistence), adab refers to acts the Prophet performed only once or twice to perfect the sunnah. The text then applies this definition to concrete actions such as hand placement, gaze positions, and suppressing natural bodily reactions, each tied to a hadith or rationale. Understanding this hierarchy helps you appreciate the Sunna’s layered nature and avoid conflating optional practices with obligatory ones.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition of adab
Read the opening sentence: 'الأدب ما فعله الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم مرة أو مرتين ولم يواظب عليه' – adab is what the Prophet did once or twice without persisting. Underline this definition.
This is the core lexical-legal claim of the whole passage.
2
Identify the purpose of adab
The text says adab was legislated 'لإكمال السنة' (to complete the sunnah). Reflect: adab does not replace sunnah but completes it, like finishing touches on a foundation.
3
Distinguish adab from other categories
Contrast adab with mustahabb (regularly performed) and sunnah mu’akkadah (emphasized sunnah). Adab is lighter and less repetitive.
The common misunderstanding is equating adab with mustahabb; the passage explicitly distinguishes them.
4
Apply the definition to the listed actions
Go through each example: hands out of sleeves, gaze positions, suppressing cough/yawn, standing at 'Hayya ala al-falah'. For each, confirm it matches the definition (done occasionally, not persisted in).
Note exceptions: a man covers hands if cold is a necessity (darura).
5
Connect to the ruling anatomy
Since adab is not wajib, its omission does not invalidate prayer. However, violating it without excuse (e.g., deliberate loud cough) may invalidate due to other rules (mufsid). Recognize the boundary.
This step prevents the student from thinking adab is compulsory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Chapter of its etiquettes (adab). Adab is what the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم did once or twice and did not persist in, such as increasing the tasbihat in bowing and prostration, and increasing over the prescribed recitation. And it is legislated to complete the sunnah. Among them: the man taking his hands out of his sleeves for the takbir of ihram due to its closeness to humility, except for necessity like cold. The woman covers her hands out of fear of exposing her forearm, and likewise the khuntha. And among them: the worshipper's gaze—whether man or woman—to the place of his prostration while standing, to preserve him from looking at what distracts from khushu'; and his gaze to the top of his foot while bowing, to the tip of his nose while prostrating, and to his lap while sitting, reflecting on the hadith: 'Worship Allah as if you see Him, for if you do not see Him, He sees you,' so he does not occupy himself with other than Him. And among them: his gaze to the shoulders when giving salam. And if he is blind or in darkness, he should contemplate the greatness of Allah. And from adab: covering his mouth when yawning, and if unable, covering it with his hand or sleeve, due to the hadith: 'Yawning in prayer is from the devil; if one of you yawns, let him suppress it as much as possible.' And from adab: standing—i.e., the people and the imam, if present, near the mihrab—at the time, i.e., when the mu'adhdhin says 'Hayya 'ala al-falah,' because he is commanded to stand, so he responds.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage opens the section on the etiquettes (adab) of prayer. The commentator defines adab as an act performed by the Prophet once or twice without regularity, distinct from mustahabb (which is done regularly but without strict continuity). The matn then lists several adab actions: taking hands out of sleeves for takbir (men) and covering hands (women), looking at specific places during different postures to maintain focus, suppressing cough and yawning, and standing when the caller says 'Hayya 'ala al-falah.' Each is supported by hadith or reasoning. The commentary emphasizes that these acts are not obligatory but enhance the prayer's completeness and humility.

Key Terms
الأدب (al-adab): In this context, a recommended act performed by the Prophet once or twice without persistence, to complete the sunnah.
الخشوع (al-khushū‘): Humility and focused presence in prayer, which is enhanced by proper gaze.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Adab in the Hanafi school refers to occasional acts of the Prophet that complete the sunnah; following them perfects prayer without imposing obligation.

Etiquette of Gaze in Prayer: A Hanafi Guide to Khushu
Commentary on adab of gaze during different prayer positions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended gaze for each prayer posture and explain the underlying prophetic evidence.

Core Idea
The worshipper's gaze during prayer directs the heart — focusing the eyes on specific points cultivates khushu' and embodies the hadith 'Worship Allah as if you see Him.'

In Hanafi fiqh, the adab (etiquette) of gaze in prayer is a practical expression of khushu' — reverent mindfulness. This lesson examines the specific postures and the prophetic proof that grounds them, distinguishing between sunnah-adab and obligatory elements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the placement of the gaze during different prayer postures. The ruling is sunnah (adab), not wajib or fard.
Sunnah adab enhances perfection but omission does not invalidate prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The main proof is the hadith: 'Worship Allah as if you see Him, for if you do not see Him, He sees you.' This is recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
This is a hadith ahad, zanni al-thubut, thus yielding recommendation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith implies constant awareness of Allah's presence. Fixing the gaze on specific points prevents distraction and promotes that awareness.
The specific points are derived from the Prophet's practice (Sunnah), not directly from the hadith.
4
Distinguish sunnah from wajib
Understand that omitting a sunnah act reduces the perfection of the prayer but does not invalidate it or require compensation. Wajib omission would require sajdah al-sahw.
This distinction is critical to avoid over-obligating the prayer.
5
Apply to all postures
List each posture's recommended gaze: standing → place of prostration; bowing → top of foot; prostrating → tip of nose; sitting → lap; salam → shoulders. For the blind or darkness, contemplate Allah's greatness.
The gaze should be steady, not wandering.

Commentary
This passage details the specific placement of the worshipper's gaze during different postures of prayer to maintain khushu'. It is recommended to look at the place of prostration while standing, at the top of the foot while bowing, at the nose while prostrating, at the lap while sitting, and at the shoulders when giving salam. These acts are classified as adab (etiquette) based on the hadith 'Worship Allah as if you see Him,' which encourages mindfulness. الحجر (al-hijr): The lap or the space between the hands in front of the body while sitting.

Etiquette of Cough, Yawn, and Standing for Iqamah
Ruling on adab of cough, yawn, and standing for iqamah with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the adab rules for cough, yawn, and standing during iqamah in salah, and identify when these actions invalidate prayer.

Core Idea
Suppress cough and yawn in prayer; stand at 'Hayya 'ala al-falah' — adab preserves salah.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi details three etiquettes of prayer: suppressing coughing to avoid invalidation, covering the mouth when yawning based on a prophetic hadith, and standing during the iqamah at the words 'Hayya 'ala al-falah'. These acts are classified as adab (recommended), but failure to observe them may affect the prayer's validity if they produce letters without excuse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three etiquettes
Read the passage and note the three actions: suppressing cough, covering mouth when yawning, and standing at 'Hayya 'ala al-falah'.
Each is introduced with 'wa min al-adab'.
2
Analyze the hadith evidence for yawning
The author cites the hadith 'Yawning in prayer is from the devil; if one of you yawns, let him suppress it as much as possible.' Understand that this indicates a recommendation (adab), not a prohibition.
The hadith is in Sahih Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Determine the impact of violating these etiquettes
The passage notes that coughing can invalidate prayer if it produces distinct letters and is without excuse. Similarly for belching (mentioned). For yawning and standing, violation does not invalidate but detracts from perfection.
The invalidation is conditional on producing letters intentionally or carelessly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And from adab: suppressing coughing as much as possible, to guard against invalidation (mufsid), for if it occurs without excuse it invalidates, and similarly belching. And from adab: covering his mouth when yawning, and if unable, covering it with his hand or sleeve, due to the hadith: 'Yawning in prayer is from the devil; if one of you yawns, let him suppress it as much as possible.' And from adab: standing—i.e., the people and the imam, if present, near the mihrab—at the time, i.e., when the mu'adhdhin says 'Hayya 'ala al-falah,' because he is commanded to stand, so he responds.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage covers three additional etiquettes. First, suppressing coughing as much as possible, since a cough that produces distinct letters without excuse invalidates the prayer; similarly, belching. Second, covering the mouth when yawning, and if yawning cannot be suppressed, covering with hand or sleeve, based on the hadith that yawning in prayer is from Shaytan. Third, standing up at the time of iqamah, specifically when the caller says 'Hayya 'ala al-falah,' as this is a command to stand for prayer. These acts are classified as adab (recommended) and enhance the propriety of prayer.

Key Terms
السعال (al-su'āl): Coughing, which can invalidate prayer if it produces letters without excuse.
الجشاء (al-jushā'): Belching, similar ruling to coughing in prayer.
التثاؤب (al-tathā'ub): Yawning, considered from Shaytan in prayer, thus to be suppressed.

In salah, suppress cough and yawn to maintain perfection; stand at 'Hayya 'ala al-falah' to respond to the call.

The Recommended Gaze During Prayer Postures
Explains recommended gaze for each posture with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended gaze for each posture in prayer and explain the hadith proof that establishes this practice as sunnah.

Core Idea
Look at the sujud spot when standing, top of foot when bowing, nose tip in sujud, lap when sitting, shoulders during salam.

Proper concentration (khushu) in prayer is enhanced by directing one's gaze appropriately. The Hanafi school specifies a recommended gaze for each posture, based on the prophetic instruction to worship Allah as if you see Him. This lesson details those gazes and the proof from hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the posture and corresponding gaze
List each posture (standing, bowing, prostrating, sitting, salam) and the recommended gaze for each as stated in the text.
2
Classify the ruling level
Recognize that these gazes are sunnah (recommended), not fard or wajib. The text uses 'ادب' (etiquette) and the commentary confirms they are to enhance khushu.
Knowing the legal level prevents over‑obligation.
3
Locate the dalil
The text cites the hadith 'اعبد الله كأنك تراه فإن لم تكن تراه فإنه يراك' (worship Allah as if you see Him…). Identify that this is a hadith (zanni al-thubut) and the proof for the gazes.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Explain the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative to worship as if seeing Allah implies focusing one's senses, including sight, on the act of worship to avoid distraction. Hence, specific gazes are recommended.
5
Note the flexibility
Understand that the gaze is recommended, not obligatory. The commentary adds that even if one is facing the Kaaba, the same etiquette is observed, and the blind person observes Allah's greatness.
The ruling accommodates necessity (e.g., fear).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو امرأة إلى موضع سجوده قائماً حفظا له عن النظر إلى ما يشغله عن الخشوع (و) نظره إلى ظاهر القدم راكعاً، وإلى أرنبة أنفه ساجداً، وإلى حجره جالساً) ملاحظاً قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «اعبد الله كأنك تراه فإن لم تكن تراه فإنه يراك فلا يشتغل بسواه (و) منها نظره إلى المنكبين مسلماً) وإذا كان بصيراً أو في ظلمة فيلاحظ عظمة الله تعالى قوله: (حذراً من کشف ذراعها أي فإنه عورة على الصحيح، وهذا في الحرة لا في الأمة. قوله : (قائماً) أي ولو حكماً كالقاعد قوله : (إلى ظاهر القدم راكعاً هذا لا يتأتى في المصلي قاعداً. قوله : (وإلى حجره) هو ما بين يديك من الثوب كما في القاموس، وهو المراد هنا، ويفعل هذا ولو كان مشاهداً للكعبة على المذهب. قوله : (كأنك تراه فإنّ العبد إذا رأى سيده أحسن طاعته . قوله: (فإن لم تكن تراه أي الرؤية المعنوية أي فلا تغفل عن عبادته فإنه يراك أفاده السعد في شرح الأربعين قوله : (وإذا كان بصيراً) أي أعمى فهو من إطلاق إسم الضد على ضده، وقوله فيلا حظ عظمة الله الأولى فيكفيه ملاحظة العظمة، وإلا فالعظمة ملاحظة لكل مصل.
Or a woman (looks) at the place of her prostration while standing, to protect herself from looking at what distracts her from khushu. And his looking at the top of the foot while bowing, at the tip of his nose while prostrating, and at his lap while sitting, noting the saying of the Prophet ﷺ: 'Worship Allah as if you see Him, for even if you do not see Him, He sees you,' so he does not occupy himself with other than it. And from it is his looking at the shoulders while saying the salam. And if he is sighted or in darkness, he should observe the greatness of Allah. He said: (Beware of uncovering her forearm, for it is 'awrah according to the correct view, and this applies to the free woman, not the slave woman.) He said: (Standing) meaning even legally, like the one sitting. He said: (At the top of the foot while bowing) this does not apply to the one praying sitting. He said: (And at his lap) it is what is in front of you of the garment, as in al-Qamus, and that is intended here, and one does this even if he is facing the Kaaba according to the madhhab. He said: (As if you see Him) for when the servant sees his master, he improves his obedience. He said: (For even if you do not see Him) meaning spiritual sight, so do not neglect His worship for He sees you. Sa'd mentioned this in Sharh al-Arba'in. He said: (And if he is sighted) meaning blind, it is calling the opposite by its opposite; and his saying: 'he should observe the greatness of Allah'—the first is sufficient for him to observe greatness, otherwise greatness is observed by every worshipper.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the recommended (mustahabb/sunnah) gaze during different postures of the prayer. The text begins by stating that a woman should look at the place of her prostration while standing, to avoid distraction. For a man (implied), the gaze is directed to the top of the foot while bowing, the tip of the nose while prostrating, the lap while sitting, and the shoulders while saying the salam. The proof is the hadith 'Worship Allah as if you see Him...' which emphasizes awareness of Allah's presence. The commentary clarifies that the gaze to the lap refers to the space in front of the garment. Even if one is facing the Kaaba, this etiquette is observed. The observation of Allah's greatness is recommended for both sighted and blind. The commentary on the woman's forearm is a separate note: it is 'awrah to uncover, and that ruling applies only to free women, not slave women.

Key Terms
أرنبة الأنف (uranat al-anf): The tip or fleshy part of the nose, which one looks at during prostration.
حجر (hijr): The lap area (the front part of the garment in front of the body while sitting).
منكبين (mankibayn): The shoulders; one looks at them during the salam.

Etiquette of Suppressing Cough and Yawning in Prayer
Explains the recommended actions to suppress cough and yawn during prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended actions for suppressing cough and yawning during prayer and explain when they may invalidate the prayer.

Core Idea
Suppressing cough and yawning in prayer is sunnah; voluntary sounds invalidate, but unavoidable ones are excused.

In this lesson, we examine the etiquette of suppressing cough (sual) and yawning (tatha'ub) during salah. The text from Maraqi al-Falah, with commentary from al-Tahtawi, outlines the recommended actions and clarifies when these acts may nullify the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts and their recommended ruling
The text states that suppressing cough and covering the mouth when yawning are part of the etiquette (adab) of prayer. These are sunnah, not obligatory.
The ruling is derived from the hadith and the general principle that excessive movement may invalidate prayer.
2
Recognize the condition for invalidation
If a cough or yawn produces letters (huruf) voluntarily without an excuse, it invalidates the prayer. Belching (jasha') is treated similarly.
The key is the production of letters; a mere sound without letters does not invalidate.
3
Examine the hadith proof for yawning
The text cites the hadith: 'Yawning in prayer is from Satan; if one of you yawns, let him suppress it as much as possible.' This indicates the recommended action.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for a sunnah ruling.
4
Note the exceptions
If suppressing the cough causes harm or distracts the heart, it is better not to suppress. Similarly, clearing the throat to remove phlegm for recitation, especially for an imam, is excused.
This shows that the ruling is not absolute; necessity ('udhr) overrides the general recommendation.
5
Understand the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds that involuntary sounds do not invalidate prayer at all, while the Hanafi school distinguishes between voluntary (invalidating if letters) and involuntary (not invalidating).
The practical difference is in cases of deliberate cough or yawn with sound.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) من الأدب (دفع السعال ما استطاع) تحرزاً عن المفسد فإنه إذا كان بغير عذر يفسد وكذا الجشاء (و) من الأدب (كظم فمه عند التثاؤب) فإن لم يقدر غطاه بيده أو كمه لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : التثاؤب في الصلاة من الشيطان فإذا تثاءب أحدكم فليكظم ما استطاع قوله: (دفع السعال ما إستطاع أي مدة إستطاعته أما إذا كان يحصل له منه ضرر، أو يشتغل قلبه بدفعه فالأولى عدم دفعه كما في تنحنح محتاج إليه لدفع بلغم منعه عن القراءة، أو عن الجهر، وهو إمام ذكره البرهان الحلبي، والسعال بالضم كما هو القياس في أسماء الأدواء حركة تدفع بها الطبيعة أذى عن الرئة، والأعضاء التي تتصل بها قوله : ( يفسد) أي إذا حصل به حروف ، ومثله الجشاء. قوله : ( كطم فمه عند التثاؤب) أي إمساكه وسده ولو بأخذ شفتيه بسنه فإن أمكنه أخذ شفتيه بسنه فلم يفعل، وغطاه بيده أو كمه كره كذا عن الإمام خلاصة، والتثاؤب إنفتاح الفم بريح يخرج من المعدة لمرض من الأمراض يحدث فيها فيوجب ذلك وقال ابن درستويه في شرح الفصيح : هو ما يصيب الإنسان عند الكسل والنعاس والهم من فتح الفم، والتمطي اهـ والأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام محفوظون منه جميعاً نهر عن شرح الشمائل لابن حجر. قوله: (فليكظم ما استطاع ليرد عليه قصده وورد أن الشيطان يضحك من ابن آدم إذا تثاءب.
And from the etiquette is (suppressing cough as much as possible) as a precaution against the invalidator, for if it is without excuse, it invalidates, and similarly belching. And from the etiquette is (covering his mouth when yawning); if he cannot, he covers it with his hand or sleeve due to his saying ﷺ: 'Yawning in prayer is from Satan; if one of you yawns, let him suppress it as much as possible.' He said: 'Suppressing cough as much as possible means for as long as he can; but if it causes him harm or his heart becomes occupied with suppressing it, then it is better not to suppress it, as in the case of clearing the throat needed to remove phlegm that prevents recitation or loudness, if he is an imam—mentioned by Burhan al-Halabi. Cough (with a damma) is, as is the measure for names of diseases, a movement by which nature repels harm from the lungs and connected organs. He said: 'It invalidates' meaning if it produces letters, and similarly belching. He said: 'Covering his mouth when yawning' means holding and closing it, even by taking his lips with his teeth; if he can take his lips with his teeth and does not do so, but covers it with his hand or sleeve, it is disliked—reported from Imam Khalasa. Yawning is the opening of the mouth with wind emanating from the stomach due to a disease that occurs therein, causing that. Ibn Darastawayh said in Sharh al-Fasih: 'It is what afflicts a person at times of laziness, drowsiness, and grief—opening the mouth and stretching.' The prophets, peace be upon them, are all protected from it—from Nahr, citing Sharh al-Shama'il by Ibn Hajar. He said: 'Let him suppress it as much as possible so that his intention returns to him, and it is reported that Satan laughs at the son of Adam when he yawns.'
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage covers two related etiquettes: suppressing cough and yawning during prayer. The ruling is that one should try to suppress cough as much as possible to avoid invalidating the prayer, since voluntary cough that produces letters (sounds) nullifies the prayer. Similarly, belching is treated like cough. For yawning, the command is to suppress it or cover the mouth, based on the hadith that yawning is from Satan. The commentary clarifies exceptions: if suppressing cough causes harm or distraction, it is better not to suppress. The commentary also defines yawning and notes that prophets are protected from it. The etiquette is sunnah, not obligatory.

Key Terms
السعال (al-su'al): Cough, a movement to expel harm from the lungs.
التثاؤب (al-tatha'ub): Yawning, opening of the mouth due to wind from the stomach, often from laziness or sleepiness.
كظم (kazm): Suppressing, holding back, e.g., covering the mouth during a yawn.

Standing Up at 'Hayya 'ala al-Falah'
Explains the recommended time for standing during iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended time for standing during iqamah and identify the intra-Hanafi difference on this point.

Core Idea
Stand at 'Hayya 'ala al-Falah' — it's a call to success, i.e., prayer.

In this passage, we learn the proper etiquette during iqamah. The key question is: when exactly should the congregation stand? The Hanafi school provides a detailed answer based on the wording of the iqamah, classifying the action as sunnah (recommended). We also see a minor difference among Hanafi imams on the precise moment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act? Standing for prayer. Its ruling is sunnah, not obligatory, as it is part of adab (etiquette).
The text begins with 'wa min al-adab' indicating it is recommended, not required.
2
Locate the proof
The proof: the phrase 'Hayya 'ala al-Falah' is a command, so it must be answered by standing. The command implies hastening to prayer.
The phrase means 'come to success', and success here is prayer.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Hasan and Zufar held that standing should be at 'Hayya 'ala al-Salah' instead. Understand their reasoning and the preferred view.
Both opinions are within the Hanafi school; the mufta bihi is the former.
4
Apply the exception for the absent imam
If the imam is not present, each row stands when the imam reaches them, not at a fixed phrase.
This shows flexibility in the ruling.
5
Note the ruling for latecomers
If someone enters the mosque during iqamah, he should sit, not stand; standing at the beginning of iqamah is disliked (makruh).
This prevents confusion with the prayer posture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) من الأدب (القيام) أي قيام القوم والإمام إن كان حاضراً بقرب المحراب حين) (قيل أي وقت قول المقيم (حي على الفلاح) لأنه أمر به فيجاب وإن لم يكن حاضراً يقوم كل صف حين ينتهي إليه الإمام في الأظهر قوله: (حي على الفلاح) وقال الحسن وزفر عند حي على الصلاة كما في سكب الأنهر عن ابن الكمال معزياً إلى الذخيرة قوله : ( لأنه أمر به فيخاب أي لأن المقيم أمر بالقيام أي ضمن قوله حي على الفلاح فإن المراد بفلاحهم المطلوب منهم حينئذ الصلاة فيبادر إليها بالقيام. قوله : ( يقوم كل صف الخ) وفي عبارة بعضهم فكلما جاوز صفاً قام ذلك الصف اهـ وإن دخل من قدامهم قاموا حين رأوه، وإذا أخذ المؤذن في الإقامة، ودخل رجل المسجد فإنه يقعد، ولا ينتظر قائماً فإنه مكروه كما في المضمرات قهستاني، ويفهم منه كراهة القيام إبتداء الإقامة والناس عنه غافلون.
And from the etiquette is (standing) meaning the standing of the people and the imam if he is present near the mihrab at the time (it is said: at the time the mu'adhdhin says 'Hayya 'ala al-Falah') because it is a command, so it is answered. And if he is not present, each row stands when the imam reaches it in the most apparent view. He said: ('Hayya 'ala al-Falah') and al-Hasan and Zufar said at 'Hayya 'ala al-Salah' as in Sakb al-Anhar from Ibn al-Kamal, attributing to al-Dhakhira. He said: (Because it is a command and is answered) meaning because the mu'adhdhin is commanded to stand, i.e., implied by his saying 'Hayya 'ala al-Falah', for the meaning of their success sought from them then is the prayer, so they hasten to it by standing. He said: (Each row stands etc.) and in the wording of some: whenever he passes a row, that row stands. And if he enters from the front, they stand when they see him. And when the mu'adhdhin begins the iqamah and a man enters the mosque, he should sit and not wait standing, for that is disliked, as in al-Mudmarat al-Qahistani. It is understood from this the dislike of standing at the beginning of the iqamah, and people are heedless of this.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage covers the etiquette of standing for prayer when the iqamah is pronounced. The preferred time for the congregation to stand is when the mu'adhdhin says 'Hayya 'ala al-Falah', not at 'Hayya 'ala al-Salah' (as stated by some). This is because the phrase 'Hayya 'ala al-Falah' is a command to come to success, which is prayer, so they respond by standing. If the imam is not present, each row stands when the imam reaches them. The commentary also notes that entering the mosque after the iqamah has started, one should sit, not stand, to avoid resembling the prayer posture prematurely—this is disliked.

Key Terms
حي على الفلاح (hayya 'ala al-falah): Come to success—a phrase in the iqamah that signals the prayer is about to begin.
محراب (mihrab): The niche indicating the qibla direction in the mosque; near it the imam stands.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, standing at 'Hayya 'ala al-Falah' is the recommended sunnah, and standing earlier is makruh.
