Beginning the Actions of Prayer: Removing Hands and Raising Them
Starts a new section detailing the order of prayer actions, beginning with removing hands from sleeves and raising them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first two actions of salah for a man according to the Hanafi school and explain the gender-based distinction.

Core Idea
Remove hands from sleeves, then raise them to ear level — but only for men; women do not remove hands.

This passage introduces the sequential actions of prayer. Before the takbir, a man must first free his hands from his sleeves, then raise them to his ears. Women follow a different rule. The precise positioning of the thumbs at the earlobes is a sunnah practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first action
What does the text say a man should do first when entering prayer? Note the phrase: 'أخرج كفيه من كميه'.
This action applies only to men.
2
Identify the second action
After removing hands, what is the next step? 'ثم رفعهما حذاء أذنيه'.
The alignment is specifically with the earlobes.
3
Apply the gender distinction
Why does the text specify 'للرجل'? What is the ruling for women?
Women do not remove hands from sleeves; the sunnah is for men.

The second action: then he raises his hands to the level of his ears, aligning his thumbs with his earlobes, and the palms face... The text cuts off. Timing of Starting Prayer After Iqamah
Ruling on when to start prayer after iqamah with ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi internal ikhtilaf on when the imam should begin the prayer after iqamah and state the mufta bihi position with its dalil.

Core Idea
The imam's start at 'qad qamat al-salah' is mustahabb, not wajib.

Knowing the precise moment to begin the congregational prayer after the iqamah is important for the imam and congregation. The Hanafi school has an internal difference of opinion on this point. This lesson unpacks the views of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf, the supporting evidence, and the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the dispute
Identify the two positions: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that the imam starts when the mu'addhin says 'qad qamat al-salah'. Abu Yusuf holds that he starts after the entire iqamah is finished.
Both are within the Hanafi school.
2
Find the common ground
Note that all three agree that if the imam delays until after the iqamah, there is no harm (la ba'sa bihi). This shows the disagreement is over the preferred time, not validity.
The disagreement is in the category of mustahabb (recommended), not wajib.
3
Analyze the dalil
The hadith of Anas (Bukhari) shows the Prophet was detained after iqamah, proving that immediate commencement is not obligatory. This refutes the claim that it is wajib and supports the view that it is mustahabb.
The dalil is a hadith ahad, which is zanni al-thubut, hence the ruling is not fard/wajib.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Later authorities (Al-Tahtawi, Sharh al-Majma', al-Khalasa) state that the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is 'a'dal al-madhahib' (the most balanced) and is the relied-upon position.
Thus the mufta bihi is to start at 'qad qamat al-salah'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if he is not present, each row stands when the imam reaches them in the most apparent view. And from the etiquette: the imam begins his ihram (i.e., before it) meaning when the mu'addhin says 'qad qamat al-salah' according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said: he begins when he finishes the iqamah. If he delays until finishing the iqamah, it is fine according to all of them. His saying: ... (then commentary)...
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage discusses the etiquette of standing for prayer and the precise moment the imam should begin the opening takbir in congregation. The base text states that the imam should start when the mu'addhin utters 'qad qamat al-salah' according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), while Abu Yusuf holds that the imam should start after the iqamah is completely finished. However, all agree that if the imam delays slightly until the end of iqamah, there is no harm. The commentary then provides further elaboration: the rows should stand as the imam passes them; it is disliked for a person entering the mosque during iqamah to remain standing; the preferred view is that the imam starts without a gap after iqamah, as held by the three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) and it is the most balanced opinion. The hadith of Anas is cited to show that the Prophet was detained after iqamah, indicating that immediate connection is not an emphasized sunnah but a recommended practice. The ikhtilaf among the Hanafi imams is thus resolved as a matter of recommendation (istihbab), not obligation.

Key Terms
الإقامة (al-iqamah): The second call to prayer immediately before the congregation begins.
شروع الإمام (shuru' al-imam): The imam's beginning of the prayer by saying Allahu Akbar (takbir al-ihram).
قد قامت الصلاة (qad qamat al-salah): The phrase in the iqamah that signals the imam to start the prayer according to the relied-upon view.
أعدل المذاهب (a'dal al-madhahib): The most balanced of the schools (opinions) — used here to refer to the preferred view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The imam must wait until all rows are perfectly aligned.

Key Takeaway
The imam should start the prayer when 'qad qamat al-salah' is said, but if he delays until the end of the iqamah, the prayer is still valid—the ikhtilaf is over mustahabb, not obligation.

Opening Acts of Prayer: Raising Hands, Takbir, and Intention
Detailed hashya on the opening acts of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on when to raise hands, how to pronounce the takbir correctly without invalidating madd, and the role of intention in initiating prayer.

Core Idea
Raising hands before takbir is preferred; excessive madd can invalidate; intention must accompany the takbir.

This lesson unpacks the detailed rulings from the hashya on the opening sequence of prayer. We examine the preferred timing of raising hands, the linguistic precision required in the takbir, and the necessity of intention as a condition. These details are crucial for the validity of the prayer from its very start.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three opening actions
The passage covers raf' al-yadayn (raising hands), the takbir (saying Allahu Akbar), and niyyah (intention). Determine the ruling for each: sunnah muakkadah for raf' and correct takbir, shart for niyyah.
2
Analyze the timing dispute for raising hands
Three views exist: before, during, or after takbir. Note the preferred view (before) and its proof: negation of greatness from others precedes affirmation for Allah.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Yusuf and al-Tahawi held during takbir.
3
Examine the rules of madd in the takbir
Prolongation (madd) can invalidate prayer if it changes the meaning, e.g., elongating the hamza of Allah creates interrogation (kufr if intentional). Understand which madd is allowed and which is corrupting.
Madd in the middle of Allah up to two harakāt is acceptable; excessive madd in 'Akbar' may create invalid meanings.
4
Recognize intention as a condition
Niyyah must accompany the takbir in legal terms. It can be slightly before as long as no foreign act intervenes. Without intention, the takbir does not enter one into prayer.
The mute person is not obligated to move their tongue for intention.
5
Apply the rulings to a scenario
Given a worshipper who raises hands after takbir, or who prolongs the hamza of Allah intentionally, determine the validity and necessary corrective actions.

Chapter on the arrangement of actions of prayer. The intended meaning of 'actions of prayer' includes its words... (then commentary on raising hands, takbir, madd, and intention)...
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This lengthy excerpt from the hashya covers the entire sequence of the opening acts of prayer. It begins by defining 'actions of prayer' as including both verbal and physical elements. The key rulings are: a man should remove his hands from his sleeves before raising them. Raising should be to the level of the ears, thumbs touching earlobes, palms facing the qibla, fingers neither spread nor clenched. If there is an excuse, he raises as much as possible. A free woman raises to her shoulders; a slave woman like a man. The commentary then discusses the wisdom of raising hands and the ikhtilaf on whether to raise before, with, or after takbir. The preferred view (al-ashah) is to raise first then say takbir, because negation of greatness from others precedes affirmation for Allah. Then the ruling on takbir: it must be said without prolongation (madd). Prolongation can invalidate the prayer if done in certain ways (e.g., elongating the first hamza of Allah creates istifham (interrogation) which is kufr if intentional). Various cases of madd are examined: in the middle of Allah is acceptable but not excessive; in the end (prolonging the ha) is a linguistic mistake but does not invalidate. For 'Akbar', elongating the first letter invalidates; elongating the middle to 'akbar' (with long alif after kaf) may create the meaning of 'drums' or 'devil's names' - some say it invalidates, others say it doesn't if it's a dialect. The ruling for the mu'adhdhin is more lenient. Finally, intention (niyyah) is a condition for the validity of takbir; one becomes a prayer-entrant only through both intention and takbir together. The intention can be made slightly before takbir as long as no foreign act separates them. The mute person is not required to move his tongue. All these details derive from the Hanafi school's reliance on hadith and linguistic precision.

Key Terms
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising both hands to the ears or shoulders during takbir al-ihram, a sunnah act.
المد (al-madd): Elongation of vowels in the takbir beyond normal length, which can invalidate prayer in certain cases.
النية (al-niyyah): Intention in the heart to perform a specific prayer, required for the takbir to be valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) During the takbir
C) Before the takbir
D) It is not required at all

Key Takeaway
The opening takbir requires proper timing of hand-raising, precise pronunciation without invalidating madd, and a concurrent intention to enter the prayer.

Elongation in the Word 'Allah' of the Takbir
Rulings on elongation of the word 'Allah' in the takbir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for elongating the beginning, middle, and end of the word 'Allah' in the takbir, and identify which invalidate the prayer.

Core Idea
Elongating the hamza of 'Allah' like an interrogation invalidates; middle elongation is disliked if excessive; end elongation is a linguistic error but valid.

The takbir is a pillar of prayer, and its pronunciation must not distort meaning. Elongation (madd) can change the word's form and, in some cases, the meaning. This lesson examines the specific cases for the word 'Allah' as detailed by Hanafi scholars, so you can avoid invalidating your prayer while understanding the gradations of ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Recognize that elongation in 'Allah' can occur at the beginning (hamza), middle (lam), or end (heh).
Each position has a different legal effect.
2
Analyze the beginning elongation
Elongating the initial hamza turns 'Allah' into an interrogative form ('Aallah?'), which invalidates the prayer. If done intentionally with the meaning of questioning, it is disbelief.
This is because the meaning changes.
3
Analyze the middle elongation
Elongating the middle lam is correct if within natural limits (two harakat). Excessive elongation is makruh tanzih (disliked) but does not invalidate prayer.
The chosen view is that it remains valid.
4
Analyze the end elongation
Elongating the heh at the end or making it sukun is a linguistic error but does not invalidate the prayer, as the meaning is not fundamentally changed.
No compensation required.
5
Summarize the practical rule
Avoid any elongation that changes the meaning (like the interrogative). For middle elongation, keep it natural; if you exceed, your prayer is still valid but you should avoid it out of caution.
The ruling is consistent across Hanafi texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (بلا مد) الحاصل أن المد في التكبير إما أن يكون في لفظ الله، أو في لفظ أكبر فإن كان في لفظ الله فإما أن يكون في أوله، أو في وسطه، أو في آخره، فإن كان في أوله كان مفسداً لأنه في صورة الإستفهام حتى لو تعمده يكفر للشك في الكبرياء وإن كان في وسطه فهو الصواب إلا أنه لا يبالغ فيه فإن بالغ زيادة على مده الطبيعي، وهو قدر حركتين كره ولا تفسد على المختار كما في ابن أمير حاج، وفي السراج أنه خلاف الأولى اهم فالكراهة للتنزيه، وإن كان في آخره بأن أشبع حركة الهاء فهو خطأ من حيث اللغة ولا تفسد به الصلاة، وكذا تسكينها كذا في الحلبي وإن كان في أكبر فإن كان في أوّله فهو خطأ مفسد للصلاة، ولا يصير به شارعاً على ما مر وإن كان في وسطه حتى صار أكبار ، فقيل : تفسد صلاته لأنه . جمع كبر وهو طبل ذو وجه واحد أو إسم من أسماء أولاد الشيطان، وفي القنية لا تفسد لأنه أشاع، وهو لغة قوم واستبعده الزيلعي بأنه لا يجوز إلا في الشعر، ولو فعله المؤذن لا تجب إعادة الأذان لأن أمر الأذان أوسع كذا في السراج وإن تعمده يكفر أي مع قصد المعنى وإلا لا، ويستغفر ويتوب مضمرات وإن كان في آخره فقيل : تفسد صلاته، وقياسه أن لا يصح الشروع به ، وقيل : لا تفسد كما في العناية وابن أمير حاج، ولو حذف المصلي، ،، أو الحالف، أو الذابح المد الذي في اللام الثانية من الجلالة، أو حذف الهاء إختلف في صحة الشروع وإنعقاد اليمين، وحل الذبيحة فلا يترك ذلك إحتياطاً أفاده السيد ومر .
His saying: (Without elongation) the summary is that elongation in the takbir either occurs in the word 'Allah' or in the word 'Akbar'. If it is in the word 'Allah', then it is either at its beginning, its middle, or its end. If at its beginning, it invalidates because it is in the form of interrogation; even if he intends it, he disbelieves due to doubt in the Majesty. If at its middle, it is correct except that he should not overdo it; if he overdoes more than its natural elongation, which is the measure of two harakat, it is disliked but does not invalidate according to the chosen view as in Ibn Amir Hajj. In al-Siraj, it is contrary to the better, so the dislike is for tanzih. If at its end by extending the movement of the heh, it is an error linguistically but the prayer is not invalidated by it, and likewise making it sukun as in al-Halabi. If it is in 'Akbar', then if at its beginning, it is an error that invalidates the prayer, and he does not become a commencer as previously. If at its middle so that it becomes 'Akbar' (with a long ba), it is said his prayer invalidates because it is the plural of 'kubr' which is a drum with one face, or a name from the names of the children of Satan. In al-Quniyah, it does not invalidate because it has become widespread and it is a language of a people. Al-Zayla'i deemed it unlikely because it is only permissible in poetry. If the muadhdhin does it, the iqamah does not need to be repeated because the matter of adhan is broader, as in al-Siraj. If he does it intentionally, he disbelieves, i.e., if he intends the meaning; otherwise no, and he should seek forgiveness and repent silently. If at its end, it is said his prayer invalidates, and by analogy he should not commence with it. And it is said it does not invalidate as in al-Inayah and Ibn Amir Hajj. If the one praying, or the one swearing, or the slaughterer omits the madd in the second lam of the Glorious Name, or omits the heh, there is difference regarding the validity of commencement, the binding of the oath, and the permissibility of the slaughtered animal. So one should not leave that as a precaution, as mentioned by al-Sayyid and others.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This section explains the rulings on elongating the letters in the takbir. The takbir must be said without elongation (madd). If one elongates the hamza in 'Allah', he does not become a praying person, and if done during prayer, it invalidates it. The analysis covers various cases: if elongation is on the first letter of 'Allah', it becomes an interrogative form, which is invalidating and could be disbelief if intentional. If on the middle letter, it is correct but should not be excessive; if excessive more than two harakat, it is makruh tanzih. If on the last letter (heh), it is a linguistic error but does not invalidate. For 'Akbar', if on the first letter, it is invalid and does not initiate prayer. If on the middle (making it 'Akbar' with a long 'ba'), it becomes a plural of 'kubr' (a drum) or a name of a devil; some say it invalidates, but in al-Quniyah it does not because it is widespread language. If done intentionally with the wrong meaning, it could be disbelief. The text also discusses omission of the madd in the second lam of the name of Allah, or omission of the heh, and the difference of opinion regarding validity. The conclusion is that one should avoid such irregularities to be safe.

Key Terms
مد (madd): Elongation of a vowel letter; here specifically referring to prolonging the pronunciation in the takbir.
حركتين (harakatayn): Two units of time; the natural length of a vowel sound.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person elongates the heh at the end of 'Allah' in the takbir, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid because it is a linguistic error
B) The prayer is valid but disliked
C) The prayer is valid and there is no issue
D) The prayer must be repeated out of caution

Key Takeaway
Elongation in the takbir only invalidates if it changes the word to a different grammatical form (like interrogative); otherwise, it is either disliked or permissible.

Salah — Prayer

Elongation in the Word 'Akbar' of the Takbir
Rulings on elongation of the word 'Akbar' in the takbir, including disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for elongating the beginning, middle, and end of the word 'Akbar' in the takbir, and explain the dispute regarding the middle elongation.

Core Idea
Elongating the first letter of 'Akbar' invalidates prayer; middle elongation is disputed among Hanafi authorities; end elongation has two opinions.

The word 'Akbar' in the takbir is particularly sensitive because elongation can change it into other words with different meanings. This lesson builds on the previous one by examining the three positions for 'Akbar', including the ikhtilaf on whether the middle elongation (making it 'Akbar' with long ba) invalidates the prayer or not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions for 'Akbar'
As with 'Allah', elongation can occur at the beginning (hamza), middle (ba), or end (ra).
Each position has its own ruling and, for the middle, a dispute.
2
Analyze the beginning elongation
Elongating the initial hamza of 'Akbar' is a mistake that invalidates the prayer and does not initiate the prayer if done at the start.
It is a clear invalidator.
3
Analyze the middle elongation
If the ba is elongated so that it becomes 'Akbar' (with a long ba), some scholars say the prayer invalidates because it becomes the plural of 'kubr' (a drum) or a name of a devil. Others say it does not invalidate because it has become a common linguistic usage.
The dispute is between al-Quniyah (no invalidation) and others (invalidation).
4
Analyze the end elongation
If the final ra is elongated, there are two opinions: some say it invalidates the prayer and the takbir does not count; others say it does not invalidate.
The text mentions al-Inayah and Ibn Amir Hajj as holding the latter.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
For beginning elongation, it is agreed to invalidate. For middle and end, the relied-upon view is that the prayer is not invalidated, but caution is advised.
The text does not explicitly tarjih, but mentions both views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (بلا مد) الحاصل أن المد في التكبير إما أن يكون في لفظ الله، أو في لفظ أكبر فإن كان في لفظ الله فإما أن يكون في أوله، أو في وسطه، أو في آخره، فإن كان في أوله كان مفسداً لأنه في صورة الإستفهام حتى لو تعمده يكفر للشك في الكبرياء وإن كان في وسطه فهو الصواب إلا أنه لا يبالغ فيه فإن بالغ زيادة على مده الطبيعي، وهو قدر حركتين كره ولا تفسد على المختار كما في ابن أمير حاج، وفي السراج أنه خلاف الأولى اهم فالكراهة للتنزيه، وإن كان في آخره بأن أشبع حركة الهاء فهو خطأ من حيث اللغة ولا تفسد به الصلاة، وكذا تسكينها كذا في الحلبي وإن كان في أكبر فإن كان في أوّله فهو خطأ مفسد للصلاة، ولا يصير به شارعاً على ما مر وإن كان في وسطه حتى صار أكبار ، فقيل : تفسد صلاته لأنه . جمع كبر وهو طبل ذو وجه واحد أو إسم من أسماء أولاد الشيطان، وفي القنية لا تفسد لأنه أشاع، وهو لغة قوم واستبعده الزيلعي بأنه لا يجوز إلا في الشعر، ولو فعله المؤذن لا تجب إعادة الأذان لأن أمر الأذان أوسع كذا في السراج وإن تعمده يكفر أي مع قصد المعنى وإلا لا، ويستغفر ويتوب مضمرات وإن كان في آخره فقيل : تفسد صلاته، وقياسه أن لا يصح الشروع به ، وقيل : لا تفسد كما في العناية وابن أمير حاج، ولو حذف المصلي، ،، أو الحالف، أو الذابح المد الذي في اللام الثانية من الجلالة، أو حذف الهاء إختلف في صحة الشروع وإنعقاد اليمين، وحل الذبيحة فلا يترك ذلك إحتياطاً أفاده السيد ومر .
His saying: (Without elongation) the summary is that elongation in the takbir either occurs in the word 'Allah' or in the word 'Akbar'. If it is in the word 'Allah', then it is either at its beginning, its middle, or its end. If at its beginning, it invalidates because it is in the form of interrogation; even if he intends it, he disbelieves due to doubt in the Majesty. If at its middle, it is correct except that he should not overdo it; if he overdoes more than its natural elongation, which is the measure of two harakat, it is disliked but does not invalidate according to the chosen view as in Ibn Amir Hajj. In al-Siraj, it is contrary to the better, so the dislike is for tanzih. If at its end by extending the movement of the heh, it is an error linguistically but the prayer is not invalidated by it, and likewise making it sukun as in al-Halabi. If it is in 'Akbar', then if at its beginning, it is an error that invalidates the prayer, and he does not become a commencer as previously. If at its middle so that it becomes 'Akbar' (with a long ba), it is said his prayer invalidates because it is the plural of 'kubr' which is a drum with one face, or a name from the names of the children of Satan. In al-Quniyah, it does not invalidate because it has become widespread and it is a language of a people. Al-Zayla'i deemed it unlikely because it is only permissible in poetry. If the muadhdhin does it, the iqamah does not need to be repeated because the matter of adhan is broader, as in al-Siraj. If he does it intentionally, he disbelieves, i.e., if he intends the meaning; otherwise no, and he should seek forgiveness and repent silently. If at its end, it is said his prayer invalidates, and by analogy he should not commence with it. And it is said it does not invalidate as in al-Inayah and Ibn Amir Hajj. If the one praying, or the one swearing, or the slaughterer omits the madd in the second lam of the Glorious Name, or omits the heh, there is difference regarding the validity of commencement, the binding of the oath, and the permissibility of the slaughtered animal. So one should not leave that as a precaution, as mentioned by al-Sayyid and others.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This section explains the rulings on elongating the letters in the takbir. The takbir must be said without elongation (madd). If one elongates the hamza in 'Allah', he does not become a praying person, and if done during prayer, it invalidates it. The analysis covers various cases: if elongation is on the first letter of 'Allah', it becomes an interrogative form, which is invalidating and could be disbelief if intentional. If on the middle letter, it is correct but should not be excessive; if excessive more than two harakat, it is makruh tanzih. If on the last letter (heh), it is a linguistic error but does not invalidate. For 'Akbar', if on the first letter, it is invalid and does not initiate prayer. If on the middle (making it 'Akbar' with a long 'ba'), it becomes a plural of 'kubr' (a drum) or a name of a devil; some say it invalidates, but in al-Quniyah it does not because it is widespread language. If done intentionally with the wrong meaning, it could be disbelief. The text also discusses omission of the madd in the second lam of the name of Allah, or omission of the heh, and the difference of opinion regarding validity. The conclusion is that one should avoid such irregularities to be safe.

Key Terms
أكبار (akbaar): Form of 'Akbar' with elongated ba; could be interpreted as a plural of 'kubr' (drum) or a name of a devil.
قنية (al-Quniyah): A Hanafi fiqh reference work (al-Fatawa al-Quniyah) known for practical rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi preferred view, if a person elongates the middle letter of 'Akbar' in the takbir, making it 'Akbaar', the prayer is:
A) Invalid and must be repeated
B) Valid but disliked
C) Valid and there is no issue
D) Invalid only if the person knew the meaning

Key Takeaway
For the word 'Akbar' in the takbir, only beginning elongation clearly invalidates; middle and end have ikhtilaf, with the mufta bihi being non-invalidation.

Omission of Madd or Heh in the Name of Allah
Rulings on omission of madd or heh in the name of Allah, affecting prayer, oath, and slaughter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the rulings when the madd in the second lam or the heh of 'Allah' is omitted, and apply the precautionary principle in cases of ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Omitting the madd or heh in 'Allah' leads to ikhtilaf in validity of prayer, oath, and slaughter; precaution requires avoiding it.

This final lesson examines a distinct issue: when a person omits the elongation (madd) in the second lam of the word 'Allah', or omits the heh entirely. Such omissions affect not only prayer but also oaths and slaughter. The Hanafi school acknowledges a difference of opinion, and the guidance is to avoid these forms out of caution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two omissions
The passage discusses two cases: (1) omitting the madd in the second lam of 'Allah', and (2) omitting the heh (the last letter) of 'Allah'.
These are distinct from elongation cases.
2
Recognize the affected actions
These omissions affect three areas: the validity of starting prayer (shurū‘), the binding of an oath, and the permissibility of slaughtered meat.
The text mentions مصلي (praying), حالف (swearing), and ذابح (slaughterer).
3
Understand the ikhtilaf
There is a difference of opinion (ikhtilaf) on whether such omissions invalidate the respective acts. The text does not detail the positions but states 'اختلف في صحة الشروع وانعقاد اليمين وحل الذبيحة'.
The precise opinions are not given; the focus is on the existence of ikhtilaf.
4
Apply the precautionary principle
Because of this ikhtilaf, one should not intentionally omit the madd or heh. The text says 'فلا يترك ذلك احتياطاً' – so one should not leave that (i.e., one should not do it) as a precaution.
Precaution is recommended to ensure validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (بلا مد) الحاصل أن المد في التكبير إما أن يكون في لفظ الله، أو في لفظ أكبر فإن كان في لفظ الله فإما أن يكون في أوله، أو في وسطه، أو في آخره، فإن كان في أوله كان مفسداً لأنه في صورة الإستفهام حتى لو تعمده يكفر للشك في الكبرياء وإن كان في وسطه فهو الصواب إلا أنه لا يبالغ فيه فإن بالغ زيادة على مده الطبيعي، وهو قدر حركتين كره ولا تفسد على المختار كما في ابن أمير حاج، وفي السراج أنه خلاف الأولى اهم فالكراهة للتنزيه، وإن كان في آخره بأن أشبع حركة الهاء فهو خطأ من حيث اللغة ولا تفسد به الصلاة، وكذا تسكينها كذا في الحلبي وإن كان في أكبر فإن كان في أوّله فهو خطأ مفسد للصلاة، ولا يصير به شارعاً على ما مر وإن كان في وسطه حتى صار أكبار ، فقيل : تفسد صلاته لأنه . جمع كبر وهو طبل ذو وجه واحد أو إسم من أسماء أولاد الشيطان، وفي القنية لا تفسد لأنه أشاع، وهو لغة قوم واستبعده الزيلعي بأنه لا يجوز إلا في الشعر، ولو فعله المؤذن لا تجب إعادة الأذان لأن أمر الأذان أوسع كذا في السراج وإن تعمده يكفر أي مع قصد المعنى وإلا لا، ويستغفر ويتوب مضمرات وإن كان في آخره فقيل : تفسد صلاته، وقياسه أن لا يصح الشروع به ، وقيل : لا تفسد كما في العناية وابن أمير حاج، ولو حذف المصلي، ،، أو الحالف، أو الذابح المد الذي في اللام الثانية من الجلالة، أو حذف الهاء إختلف في صحة الشروع وإنعقاد اليمين، وحل الذبيحة فلا يترك ذلك إحتياطاً أفاده السيد ومر .
His saying: (Without elongation) the summary is that elongation in the takbir either occurs in the word 'Allah' or in the word 'Akbar'. If it is in the word 'Allah', then it is either at its beginning, its middle, or its end. If at its beginning, it invalidates because it is in the form of interrogation; even if he intends it, he disbelieves due to doubt in the Majesty. D) It does not matter because the act is still valid

Key Takeaway
When Hanafi scholars differ on a ruling without a clear tarjih, the recommended approach is precaution (ihtiyāt), especially in matters involving the name of Allah.

Intention and Commencement of Prayer: Takbir, Dhikr, and the Persian Language Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of commencing prayer with non-Arabic dhikr and recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for commencing prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding recitation in Persian.

Core Idea
Prayer begins with intention and takbir together; other dhikr suffices but is makruh; Persian is valid only if unable to speak Arabic.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's commentary on Maraqi al-Falah clarifies the foundational rules for starting prayer. It addresses three key points: the necessity of both intention and takbir, the permissibility of commencing with any pure form of remembrance, and the contentious issue of using non-Arabic (specifically Persian) for the takbir and Quranic recitation. Understanding these rulings protects the validity of one's prayer and highlights an important intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions for commencement
The text states that one becomes a 'commencer' (shari') through both intention (niyyah) and the takbir (saying Allahu Akbar). Neither alone suffices. The intention may precede the takbir if no foreign action separates them, but delaying intention after takbir is not permitted. For a mute person, tongue movement is not required.
This is the Hanafi position; other schools differ on whether takbir is a rukn.
2
Analyze the ruling on starting with pure dhikr
It is valid to commence prayer with any pure dhikr (e.g., Subhanallah, La ilaha illallah, Alhamdulillah), but this is makruh tahrimi if one is able to say the takbir in Arabic. The dhikr must be a complete sentence. This shows that the takbir is the wajib form, and leaving it is prohibitively disliked.
The Hanafi school considers the opening takbir wajib, not a rukn.
3
Examine the ruling on using Persian for the opening
It is valid to commence prayer in Persian or any other language if the person is incapable of Arabic. If capable, it is not valid. The same applies to the entire prayer: reciting in Persian is the point of dispute.
The dispute specifically concerns recitation of Quran, not the opening dhikr alone.
4
Study the intra-Hanafi dispute on reciting Quran in Persian
Abu Hanifa holds that reciting Quran in Persian is invalid because Quran is the Arabic composition and meaning together. His two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, hold that it is valid for someone unable to speak Arabic. The fatwa is on Abu Hanifa's view.
The thamarah al-khilaf: a non-Arab who prays using Persian translation has an invalid prayer unless he cannot speak Arabic.
5
Contrast with other acts of worship
The passage notes that for other acts like talbiyah (Hajj), taslim (ending prayer), tasmiyah (slaughter), and oaths, using non-Arabic is permissible by consensus even if one can speak Arabic. This exception shows that the strict ruling is specific to Quranic recitation in prayer.
This prevents overgeneralizing the ruling to all acts of worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ناوياً) اعلم أنه يصير شارعاً بالنية عند التكبير لا به وحده ولا بها وحدها، بل بهما وصح تقديمها عليه حيث لم يفصل بينهما بأجنبي للمقارنة حكماً لا تأخيرها، ولا يلزم العاجز عن النطق بها كالأخرس تحريك لسانه وكذا في حتى القراءة هو الصحيح لتعذر الواجب فلا يلزم غيره إلا بدليل در . قوله : (ويصح الشروع بكل ذكر) وفيه إشارة إلى أنه لا بد لصحة الشروع من جملة تامة (كسبحان الله أو لا إله إلا الله، أو الحمد الله (و) يصح الشروع أيضاً (بالفارسية) وغيرها من الألسن إن عجز عن العربية وإن قدر لا يصح شروعه بالفارسية ونحوها (ولا قراءته بها في الأصح في قول الإمام الأعظم موافقة لهما لأن القرآن اسم للنظم والمعنى جميعاً وأما التلبية في الحج والسلامة من الصلاة والتسمية على الذبيحة والأيمان فجائز بغير العربية القدرة عليها إجماعاً
His saying: (Intending) Know that he becomes a commencer with the intention at the time of the takbir, not by the takbir alone nor by the intention alone, but by both. And it is correct to precede it over the takbir as long as nothing foreign separates them, for legal simultaneity; not to delay it. And the one incapable of pronouncing it, like the mute, is not required to move his tongue, and likewise in even the recitation, that is the correct ruling because the obligatory is unfeasible, so nothing else is required except by evidence. His saying: (And it is valid to commence with any remembrance) And in it is an indication that for the validity of commencement, a complete sentence is necessary, like 'Subhanallah' or 'La ilaha illallah' or 'Alhamdulillah'. And it is valid to commence also (in Persian) and other languages if he is incapable of Arabic. And if he is able, his commencement in Persian and the like is not valid. (And not to recite it in it) is the most correct according to the statement of the Greatest Imam, in agreement with his two companions, because the Quran is the name for the composition and the meaning together. As for the talbiyah in Hajj, and the taslim from prayer, and the tasmiyah over the slaughtered animal, and oaths, it is permissible in other than Arabic even with the ability upon it, by consensus.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage discusses the conditions for commencing prayer. The prayer begins with the intention (niyyah) at the time of takbir; neither alone suffices. The intention may precede the takbir as long as there is no foreign interval. For one unable to speak (like a mute), moving the tongue is not required. The text then states that it is valid to start with any pure remembrance of Allah, such as 'Subhanallah', 'La ilaha illallah', or 'Alhamdulillah', though it is makruh tahrimi for leaving the wajib (the takbir). This indicates that a complete sentence is necessary. It is also valid to start in Persian or other languages if one is unable to speak Arabic. If able, starting in Persian is not valid. The dispute arises over reciting the Quran in non-Arabic: in the most correct opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa, it is not valid because the Quran is both the words and the meaning. His two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that it is valid for one unable to speak Arabic. The fatwa is on Abu Hanifa's view. However, for talbiyah in Hajj, and taslim in prayer, and tasmiyah on slaughter, and oaths, using non-Arabic is permissible even if one can speak Arabic, by consensus.

Key Terms
ناوياً (nāwiyan): Intending; the condition of having intention at the time of takbir for the prayer to be valid.
ذكر خالص (dhikr khāliṣ): Pure remembrance of Allah, free from any worldly request.
التكبير (al-takbīr): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' to commence the prayer (takbirat al-ihram).
الفارسية (al-fārisiyya): The Persian language; used here as an example of a non-Arabic language.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a person who is able to speak Arabic but starts his prayer with 'Subhanallah' instead of 'Allahu Akbar'?
A) The prayer is invalid because takbir is a rukn.
B) The prayer is valid and recommended.
C) The prayer is valid but makruh tahrimi.
D) The prayer is invalid because intention is missing.

Key Takeaway
Prayer commences with both intention and the takbir; any pure dhikr suffices but is disliked if the takbir is possible, and non-Arabic is only valid for those unable to speak Arabic, with the intra-Hanafi dispute resolved on Abu Hanifa's view.

Hand Placement and Opening Supplication in Prayer
Ruling on hand placement and opening supplication

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on hand placement and the opening supplication in the Hanafi school, and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the basis of hand placement.

Core Idea
Placing hands under navel and reciting Subhanakallahumma are sunnah muakkadah, not obligatory.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya explains the ruling on hand placement immediately after the takbir and the recited opening supplication. It clarifies that these acts are sunnah muakkadah and there is an intra-Hanafi difference on whether hand placement is sunnah of standing or recitation. Understanding this helps in proper prayer without unnecessary invalidation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being described (placing right hand over left under navel) and its hukm level (sunnah muakkadah). Verify that omitting it does not invalidate prayer.
2
Note the timing and manner
The hands are placed immediately after the takbir (tahrimah) without delay. The opening supplication 'Subhanakallahumma...' is recited quietly.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Understand the difference: Muhammad says it is sunnah of recitation (so release hands during thana); Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (second view) say place hands in every standing with sunnah dhikr; the apparent madhhab says it is sunnah of qiyam (hands placed throughout).
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that hand placement is sunnah of qiyam, so hands remain placed throughout the standing acts of prayer (including thana, qunut, funeral prayer).
5
Apply: consequences of omission
Since it is sunnah muakkadah, omitting it does not invalidate prayer nor require sujud al-sahw. However, it is meritorious to perform.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم وضع يمينه على يساره) وتقدم صفته (تحت سرته عقیب التحريمة بلا (مهلة لأنه سنة القيام في ظاهر المذهب وعند محمد سنة القراءة، فيرسل حال الثناء وعندهما يعتمد في كل قيام فيه ذكر مسنون كحالة الثناء والقنوت وصلاة الجنازة ويرسل بين تكبيرات العيدين إذ ليس فيه ذكر مسنون (مستفتحاً، وهو أن يقول سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك، وتبارك اسمك وتعالى جدك ولا إله غيرك وإن قال وجل ثناؤك لم يمنع
Then he places his right hand on his left) and its description has preceded (under his navel immediately after the tahrimah without delay because it is sunnah of standing in the apparent madhhab. According to Muhammad, it is sunnah of recitation, so he releases it during the thana. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he relies (places) in every standing that contains a sunnah dhikr like during thana, qunut, and funeral prayer, and releases between the takbirs of the two 'Eids because there is no sunnah dhikr there. (Opening) which is that he says: Subhanakallahumma wa bihamdika, wa tabarakasmuka, wa ta'ala jadduka, wa la ilaha ghayruk. And if he says 'wa jalla thanauk', it is not prevented.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This part covers the ruling on placing the right hand over the left under the navel immediately after the takbir without delay. This is sunnah in the standing position according to the apparent madhhab. According to Muhammad, it is sunnah of recitation, so he releases his hands during the thana (subhanakallahumma). According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), one places his hands in every standing that contains a sunnah dhikr, like thana, qunut, and funeral prayer, and releases between the takbirs of Eid because there is no sunnah dhikr there. Then the opening supplication (istiftah) is recited: 'Subhanakallahumma wa bihamdika, wa tabarakasmuka, wa ta'ala jadduka, wa la ilaha ghayruk.' If one says 'wa jalla thanauk', it is not prevented.

Key Terms
وضع اليمين على اليسار (wad' al-yamīn 'alā al-yasār): Placing the right hand over the left hand under the navel during prayer.
مستفتحاً (mustaftiḥan): The opening supplication recited after the takbir, beginning with 'Subhanakallahumma...'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent madhhab of the Hanafi school, when should one place the right hand over the left under the navel?
A) After the takbir without delay
B) Only during recitation
C) Only during the opening supplication
D) Not at any specific time

Key Takeaway
Placing hands under navel immediately after takbir and reciting the opening supplication are sunnah muakkadah in the Hanafi school; the mufta bihi is that hand placement is sunnah of qiyam.

Hand Placement After Takbir: Timing and Ruling
Ruling on hand placement after opening takbir and its timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hand placement in prayer and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and the Sahibayn regarding its timing.

Core Idea
Hand placement after takbir is sunnah of qiyam, but its timing differs among the three Hanafi masters.

The placement of hands after the opening takbir is a well-known practice in prayer. In this passage, al-Tahtawi clarifies a subtle intra-Hanafi difference: is it an immediate sunnah of standing, or should it wait until after the opening supplication? Understanding this distinction sharpens your awareness of how Hanafi imams derived rulings from the same principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is placing the right hand over the left under the navel after the opening takbir. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
It is not wajib; omission does not invalidate the prayer.
2
Distinguish the three Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa: place immediately after takbir as sunnah of standing. Muhammad: place after thana' as sunnah of recitation. Sahibayn: rest hands in any standing that includes supererogatory dhikr, release otherwise.
The difference stems from whether the act is tied to qiyam or to recitation.
3
Identify the mufta bihi (operative position)
The relied-upon view (zahir al-riwaya) is Abu Hanifa's: immediate placement without delay.
Al-Tahtawi confirms this is the apparent madhhab.
4
Apply the ruling to other prayer situations
According to Sahibayn, hands are kept in qunut, janazah, and thana', but released between Eid takbirs because no supererogatory dhikr exists there.
This shows how the 'sunnah of standing' principle is applied consistently.

Source Text

ثم وضع يمينه على يساره تحت سرته عقيب التحريمة بلا مهلة لأنه سنة القيام في ظاهر المذهب وعند محمد سنة القراءة فيرسل حال الثناء وعندهما يعتمد في كل قيام فيه ذكر مسنون كحالة الثناء والقنوت وصلاة الجنازة ويرسل بين تكبيرات العيدين إذ ليس فيه ذكر مسنون قوله بلا مهلة يفتح الميم أي تراخ وبضمها عكارة الزيت قوله في كل قيام أي له قرار
Then he places his right hand on his left under his navel immediately after the tahrimah without delay, because it is the sunnah of standing in the apparent madhhab; according to Muhammad it is sunnah of recitation, so he releases during the thana'; according to them both, he leans in every standing that contains a supererogatory dhikr like the state of thana', qunut, and janazah prayer, and he releases between the takbirs of the two Eids because there is no supererogatory dhikr. He said: 'without delay' with fatha of the mim meaning laxity, and with damm it is the dregs of oil. He said: 'in every standing' meaning a settled one.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This ruling discusses the placement of the hands after the opening takbir (tahrimah). The matn states that the right hand is placed over the left under the navel immediately without delay. The commentary explains that this act is a sunnah of standing (qiyam) according to the apparent madhhab (i.e., Abu Hanifa's view). Imam Muhammad, however, considers it a sunnah of recitation, so he advises releasing the hands during the thana' (opening supplication). The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) agree that one should rest the hands in every standing that contains a supererogatory dhikr, such as during thana', qunut, and the janazah prayer, but release them between the Eid takbirs since no such dhikr occurs. The commentator clarifies linguistic points: 'bila muhlah' means without delay, and 'qiyam' here means a settled standing.

Key Terms
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir which renders worldly actions forbidden during prayer.
ثناء (thana'): The opening supplication (istiftah) recited after the takbir, also called Subhanaka.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Only during qunut and janazah prayer.
D) Between the takbirs of Eid prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position is to place hands under navel immediately after takbir, but this is sunnah, not wajib; the timing difference among imams is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

The Ruling of the Opening Supplication (Istiftah)
Explanation of the ruling of istiftah and the condition for the follower.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting istiftah for the follower and identify the condition that changes this ruling.

Core Idea
The istiftah is sunnah for every worshipper, but the follower omits it if the imam begins recitation.

The opening supplication (istiftah) is recited after the takbir. The Hanafi school holds that it is sunnah for the imam, the follower, and the one praying alone. However, the follower is required to listen to the imam's recitation; therefore, if the imam begins reciting before the follower finishes the istiftah, the follower should stop and listen. This lesson explains this ruling and its conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
Recognize that the istiftah is a sunnah act of prayer, not wajib. Its omission does not invalidate the prayer.
Sunnah acts are those for which there is reward but no sin in leaving.
2
Identify who recites it
According to the text, every person in prayer recites istiftah, whether imam, follower, or alone. This is the general rule.
The text says: 'يستفتح كل مصل سواء المقتدي وغيره'
3
Identify the exception for the follower
The follower does not recite istiftah if the imam has already begun recitation (in a loud prayer). The condition is 'what لم يبدأ الإمام بالقراءة' (unless the imam begins recitation).
This condition applies even if the imam recites quietly according to the relied-upon view.

Opening with the supplication which is to say: 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika wa tabaraka ismuka wa ta'ala jadduka wa la ilaha ghayruk' and if he says 'wa jalla thana'uka' it does not prevent. And if he remains silent, he is not commanded, and he does not bring the du'a of tawajjuh neither before nor after shuru', and he includes it in tahajjud for istiftah. His statement: 'in majesty and beauty' is related to 'pinnacle' or 'perfection'. His statement: 'and all actions' is an apposition to 'majesty', i.e., and to the pinnacle of perfection in all actions. His statement: 'and it is the absolute uniqueness' the pronoun refers to the pinnacle, and it is masculine because of the predicate. His statement: 'and what pertains to it' is an apposition to 'uniqueness' and it is specific. Commentary
This passage explains the opening supplication (istiftah) and its ruling. The matn states that every person in prayer, whether imam, follower, or alone, recites the istiftah unless the imam starts the recitation (in a loud prayer). The follower then remains silent. The Meaning and Significance of the Opening Supplication
Linguistic and theological commentary on the istiftah du'a.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the linguistic and theological meaning of each phrase in the Hanafi istiftah du'a.

Core Idea
The istiftah du'a progresses from declaring Allah's transcendence to affirming His perfection and culminates in the declaration of His exclusive divinity.

The opening supplication is not merely a formula; it encapsulates core Islamic theology. This lesson breaks down each phrase: 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika' (declaring Allah free from imperfection and praising Him), 'wa tabaraka ismuka' (the blessedness of His name), 'wa ta'ala jadduka' (the exaltation of His majesty), and 'wa la ilaha ghayruk' (the uniqueness of His divinity). The commentary highlights the semantic richness and the intended ascent in praise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key phrases
The du'a consists of four main parts: 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika', 'wa tabaraka ismuka', 'wa ta'ala jadduka', and 'wa la ilaha ghayruk'. Recognize each as a distinct statement.
Some versions add 'wa jalla thana'uka', but this is optional.
2
Analyze the first phrase: 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika'
'Subhan' is a verbal noun meaning acquittal and purity. It indicates declaring Allah free from all deficiencies. The construction 'Subhanaka' means 'I declare You free from imperfection' (with an implied verb). 'Wa bihamdika' means 'and with Your praise' – the 'ba' can indicate accompaniment or association.
It is narrated that dropping the 'waw' (saying 'bi hamdika' directly) is permissible.
3
Analyze the remaining phrases
'Tabaraka' is a non-conjugated verb meaning 'blessed' – it indicates permanence and abundance of good. 'Ta'ala jadduka' uses 'jadd' meaning majesty/supremacy, thus 'exalted is Your majesty'. 'La ilaha ghayrak' is the negation of any true deity besides Allah.
The commentary notes that these phrases progress from negative attributes (tanzih) to positive attributes (tahmid) to the ultimate tawhid.
4
Synthesize the theological ascent
The du'a begins with tanzih (declaring Allah free from imperfection), then affirms praise (tahmid), then mentions the blessedness of His names, then the exaltation of His majesty, and finally the exclusivity of His divinity. This is an ascent (tarqiya) in praise.
This structure is deliberate: starting with what Allah is not, moving to what He is, and ending with the essence of tawhid.

Source Text

مطرود عن حضرة الله تعالى ويريد أن يجعلك شريكاً له في العقاب وأنت لا تراه فتعتصم بمن يراه ليحفظك منه بالتعوذ مطلقاً وإن سكت لا يؤمر ولا يأتي بدعاء التوجه لا قبل الشروع ولا بعده ويضمه في التهجد للاستفتاح ومعنى سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك نزهتك عن صفات النقص بالتسبيح وأثبت صفات الكمال لذاتك بالتحميد وتبارك أي دام وثبت وتنزه اسمك وتعالى جدك أي ارتفع سلطانك وعظمتك وغناك بمكانتك ولا إله غيرك في الوجود رأيه أنه إن
Opening with the supplication which is to say: 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika wa tabaraka ismuka wa ta'ala jadduka wa la ilaha ghayruk' and if he says 'wa jalla thana'uka' it does not prevent. And every person in prayer recites istiftah, whether follower or other, unless the imam begins recitation. Then he seeks refuge with Allah from the accursed Shaytan, because he is expelled from the presence of Allah and he wants to make you a partner with him in punishment while you do not see him, so you seek protection from the One who sees him to protect you from him by seeking refuge absolutely. And if he remains silent, he is not commanded, and he does not bring the du'a of tawajjuh neither before nor after shuru', and he includes it in tahajjud for istiftah. And the meaning of 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika': I declare you free from attributes of deficiency by tasbih and I affirm attributes of perfection for Your essence by tahmid. 'Tabaraka' means perpetual and established. 'Ta'ala jadduka' meaning exalted is Your sovereignty, greatness, and self-sufficiency. 'La ilaha ghayruk' there is no object of worship with right except You. He began with tanzih which relates to tawhid, then ended with tawhid, rising in praise of Allah from mentioning negative attributes and positive attributes to the pinnacle of perfection in majesty, beauty, and all actions. And it is the absolute uniqueness of divinity and what pertains to it of Oneness and Self-sufficiency. His statement: 'and he includes it in tahajjud for istiftah' indicates, as is apparent, that istiftah is preceded. His statement: 'and the meaning of Subhanak' Subhan originally is a verbal noun, it has no verb, and its meaning is acquittal and purity; from 'sabaha fi al-ard' meaning he went; then it assumed the meaning of tasbih which is tanzih, and it is sometimes used as a proper noun so it is not declined due to being a proper noun and the extra alif and nun, and it is hardly used except in construction, and the accusative of Subhan is by a deleted verb that is obligatory to delete, either from its own wording (the original construction: 'sabbahatuka subhanah') or from other wording (meaning 'I believe in your subhan'), i.e., your purity from anything unbecoming of you, so on this it is a direct object not an adverb. His statement: 'wa bihamdika' is related to a deleted element, and the waw is either for connecting two sentences, the first is deleted and the connective remains, meaning 'I glorify you and begin with your praise' or 'I describe you with your praise', and it should not be said that it is superfluous because that is not regular as in al-Qahistani. It is narrated from the Imam that if he said 'Subhanaka Allahumma bihamdika' without the waw, it is permissible, and the ba' is for association, i.e., I glorify you with a glorification associated with your praise. His statement: 'wa tabaraka' is a verb that is not conjugated and is only used for Allah ta'ala, from barakah which is permanent abundant good, meaning the good of your beautiful names has multiplied, derived from water settling in the basin (i.e., permanence) or from the kneeling of camels (firmness). His statement: 'wa tanzaha' this is not from the meaning of tabaraka. His statement: 'wa ta'ala jadduka' al-jadd with fatha of jim is used for grandfather, riverbank, and majesty and grandeur, which is intended here, meaning that Your majesty is higher than the majesty of others. His statement: 'he began with tanzih' i.e., complete tanzih. His statement: 'from mentioning the attributes etc.' is related to 'rising', and likewise 'to the pinnacle of perfection'. His statement: 'in majesty and beauty' is related to 'pinnacle' or 'perfection'. His statement: 'and all actions' is an apposition to 'majesty', i.e., and to the pinnacle of perfection in all actions. His statement: 'and it is the absolute uniqueness' the pronoun refers to the pinnacle, and it is masculine because of the predicate. His statement: 'and what pertains to it' is an apposition to 'uniqueness' and it is specific. His statement: 'unless the imam begins recitation' even if quietly according to the relied-upon view, and if he catches up with him bowing, it applies if his predominant opinion is that he...
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage explains the opening supplication (istiftah) and its ruling. The matn states that every person in prayer, whether imam, follower, or alone, recites the istiftah unless the imam starts the recitation (in a loud prayer). The follower then remains silent. The commentary then delves into the linguistic and theological meanings of the words. The du'a begins with tanzih (declaring Allah free from imperfections), moves to affirmation of perfect attributes, and culminates in tawhid. The commentary analyzes each term: 'Subhan' is a verbal noun indicating acquittal; 'bihamdika' means accompanied by praise; 'tabaraka' indicates permanence and abundance of good; 'ta'ala jadduka' means exaltation of majesty. It also notes a narration from the Imam that dropping the waw is permissible. The ruling that the follower recites istiftah unless the imam has begun recitation is emphasized, and the authority states that this applies even if the imam recites quietly. The commentary ends with a note about catching up with the imam in ruku', but the text cuts off.

Key Terms
تنزيه (tanzih): Declaring Allah free from all imperfections, as expressed by 'Subhanaka'.
تحميد (tahmid): Affirming praise and perfection for Allah, as expressed by 'wa bihamdika'.
توحيد (tawhid): The affirmation of Allah's exclusive divinity, expressed by 'la ilaha ghayruk'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary in this lesson, the istiftah du'a begins with tanzih and ends with tawhid. Which phrase represents tawhid?
A) Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika
B) Wa tabaraka ismuka
C) Wa ta'ala jadduka
D) Wa la ilaha ghayruk

Key Takeaway
The istiftah du'a is a theologically rich invocation that moves from declaring Allah's transcendence to affirming His perfections and culminates in tawhid.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Meaning and Ruling of the Opening Supplication (Dua al-Tawajjuh)
Tahtawi's critical refinement on the meaning and ruling of Subhanaka.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the meaning of 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika', explain its inclusion in the tahajjud prayer, and identify its Hanafi ruling as sunnah.

Core Idea
The opening supplication is sunnah, not wajib; its meaning declares Allah's transcendence and perfection.

This lesson explores the meaning and ruling of the opening supplication (dua al-tawajjuh) recited after the takbirat al-ihram. Using Tahtawi's commentary on Maraqi al-Falah, we examine why it is sunnah, when it is included (especially in tahajjud), and the rich theological meaning of the words 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the hukm level of the opening supplication according to the Hanafi school. The text implies it is sunnah, not wajib. Look for phrases like 'la yu&#x27;mar' (is not commanded) and context.
The ruling is sunnah muakkadah; omission does not invalidate prayer.
2
Determine the occasion of inclusion
Note when the supplication is included: the text says 'wa yadummuhu fi al-tahajjud li al-istiftah' (he includes it in tahajjud for the opening). Understand that in regular prayers, it is not recited if the imam remains silent; rather he should be quiet.
In tahajjud, the supplication precedes the recitation.
3
Analyze the linguistic structure
Break down 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika': 'Subhan' is a verbal noun indicating transcendence; 'Allahumma' is a vocative; 'wa bihamdika' means 'and with Your praise'. Note the commentary on the waw and the possibility of dropping it.
Abu Hanifa allowed omission of the waw: 'Subhanaka Allahumma bihamdika'.
4
Unpack the theological meaning
The phrase combines negative attributes (tanzih) and positive attributes (tahmid). It begins with declaring Allah free from deficiency and ends with affirming perfection and uniqueness.
This progression from tanzih to tawhid is noted in the text.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi variation
The text narrates from Imam Abu Hanifa that omitting the waw is permissible. Identify the mufta bihi (preferred) position: the standard wording with waw is recommended, but both are valid.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.

If he remains silent, he is not commanded, and he does not come with the supplication of attention (dua al-tawajjuh) neither before commencing nor after, and he includes it in tahajjud for the opening. The meaning of 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika': I declare You free from attributes of deficiency by glorification, and I affirm attributes of perfection for Your essence by praise. 'Tabaraka' means enduring and established. 'Wa ta'ala jadduka' means exalted is Your sovereignty, greatness, and self-sufficiency. There is no deity worthy of worship except You. He began with tanzih, which leads to tawhid, then concluded with tawhid, progressing in praise of Allah from negative attributes and positive attributes to the ultimate perfection in majesty, beauty, and all actions. It is the unique possession of divinity and what is specific to Him of oneness and self-subsistence. The commentator says: 'He includes it in tahajjud for the opening' indicates that what is apparent is to give precedence to the opening invocation over it. The commentator says: 'The meaning of Subhanaka': Subhan originally is a verbal noun with no verb, meaning innocence and purity. It is derived from 'sabaha fil-ard' meaning went away, then it came to imply glorification. It is used as a proper noun, so it is uninflected due to being a proper noun and having the extra alif and nun. It is almost always used in the construct state, and it is in the accusative case by an omitted verb that must be omitted. 'Wa bihamdika' is connected to an omitted element. The waw is either for linking a sentence to a deleted sentence, meaning 'I glorify You and begin with Your praise,' or 'I describe You with praise.' It should not be considered extra. It is narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that if one says 'Subhanaka Allahumma bihamdika' without the waw, it is permissible. 'Tabaraka' is a verb that is not conjugated and is only used for Allah, meaning enduring and abundant goodness. 'Wa ta'ala jadduka': jadd can mean grandfather, riverbank, or greatness; here it means greatness. He began with tanzih, i.e., complete tanzih. The phrase 'from mentioning negative and positive attributes' is attached to 'progressing', and similarly till the ultimate perfection. 'In majesty and beauty' is related to 'ultimate' or 'perfection'. 'And all actions' is an appendage to 'majesty'. The pronoun in 'He is the unique possession' refers to the ultimate perfection, and 'what is specific to Him' is appended to 'unique possession'.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah, explaining the meaning and ruling of the opening supplication (dua al-istiftah). The main text states that if the imam remains silent (between the opening takbir and the Fatiha), he is not ordered to recite the opening supplication; rather, he should be quiet. The supplication (only Subhanaka) is not recited before starting the prayer nor after, but it is included in the tahajjud prayer for the purpose of istiftah (opening). Tahtawi then provides a detailed linguistic and theological explanation of 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika'. He clarifies that 'Subhan' is a verbal noun indicating transcendence; the phrase declares Allah free from all imperfections and affirms His perfect attributes. 'Tabaraka' is used exclusively for Allah, meaning perpetual and established goodness. 'Ta'ala jadduka' means Your majesty is exalted. The overall structure is a progression from tanzih (negative attributes) to tawhid (oneness), culminating in the ultimate perfection of majesty and beauty. The commentary on 'we use it in the opening of tahajjud' indicates that the opening supplication precedes the recitation in tahajjud. This clarifies the proper placement of the supplication in voluntary prayers at night.

Key Terms
دعاء التوجه (dua al-tawajjuh): The opening supplication recited after the takbirat al-ihram, also called dua al-istiftah.
التنزيه (al-tanzih): Declaring Allah free from all imperfections and negative attributes.
التسبيح (al-tasbih): Glorifying Allah by declaring Him transcendent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) After the Fatiha
D) In every rak'ah

Key Takeaway
The opening supplication (Subhanaka...) is sunnah, recited after takbir; it is particularly included in the tahajjud prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Rulings on Ta'awwudh, Tasmiyah, and Ruku'
Rulings on seeking refuge, basmala, and bowing with evidences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, and ruku' including the prohibition of Quran recitation, and identify the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Ta'awwudh and tasmiyah are sunnah before Fatiha; reciting Quran in ruku' is makruh due to explicit prohibition.

In this passage, the author presents the rulings on the opening acts of prayer: seeking refuge (ta'awwudh), saying the basmala (tasmiyah), and the bowing posture (ruku'). The text provides the evidence for prohibiting Quran recitation in ruku' and sujud, and discusses disagreements among scholars, including an intra-Hanafi difference on whether the muqtadi should recite tasmiyah. By studying this passage, you will learn the correct Hanafi positions and their proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
First, note each act (ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, ruku' tasbih, Quran recitation in ruku') and its legal classification: sunnah, wajib, or makruh.
The text explicitly states rulings: ta'awwudh and tasmiyah are sunnah, ruku' tasbih three times is the minimum perfection (sunnah), and Quran recitation in ruku' is makruh.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith cited: 'I was forbidden to recite while bowing or prostrating.' This is the primary evidence for the prohibition.
The hadith is ahad, so its transmission is zanni; but its meaning is clear and binding.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the prohibition (nahy) in the hadith leads to the ruling of karahah. The explicit command not to recite indicates that doing so is disliked (makruh tahrimi).
The Hanafi usul principle: nahy mutlaq indicates prohibition (tahrim) unless there is evidence to lower it to tanzih. Here consensus reduces it to makruh.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf holds that the muqtadi should recite tasmiyah following the thana, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say no. Also note the external dispute: al-Nakha'i and others say ta'awwudh is said after the Fatiha, not before.
These ikhtilafat are resolved by tarjih: the text sides with the majority Hanafi view.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Consider why the mufta bihi position is that the muqtadi does not recite tasmiyah: because he does not recite the Fatiha at all. The ta'awwudh and tasmiyah are for the reciter, and the muqtadi follows the imam's recitation.
The text explicitly says 'la al-muqtadi' (not the follower), rejecting Abu Yusuf's view.

بين الركعة الأولى والثانية قوله : (ذكر له يكفي أفراد الضمير بإعتبار المذكور والأفضل في الوضوء التسمية على الوجه المتقدم فيه وفي الذبيحة بإسم الله الله أكبر. قوله : (للسورة) تقييده بالسورة يفيد الكراهة إذا أتى بها للآيات قوله: (من المفصل على ما تقدم) أي من الطوال، والأوساط والقصار قوله : ( ويكره) قراءة القرآن في الركوع والسجود، والتشهد) وأما الأدعية التي في التشهد بألفاظ القرآن ينوي بها الدعاء لا القراءة وإلا كره تحريماً. قوله:
Then seek refuge in Allah from the accursed Shaytan because he is expelled from the presence of Allah and wants to make you his partner in punishment while you do not see him, so you seek protection from Him who sees him to protect you from him by seeking refuge universally. (Secretly for recitation) preceding it, so the one who is caught up (masbuq) comes with it at the beginning of what he makes up after thana (praise), for he says thana during his following (the imam), even in the imam's pauses as has been said, and he does not come with it in ruku', and he comes with it (the takbirat of the two Eids) due to their obligation. (Not the muqtadi) because it is for recitation and the muqtadi does not recite. Abu Yusuf said: He is a follower of thana, so he comes with it and delays the ta'awwudh after the additional takbirs during the two Eids because it is for recitation, and those are after the takbirs in the first rak'ah. Then he says the tasmiyah secretly as before. And every person who recites in his prayer says it in every rak'ah, whether obligatory or voluntary, before the Fatiha by saying 'Allah al-Rahman al-Rahim'. As for wudu and dhabiha, it is not restricted to the particular basmala; rather any dhikr is sufficient. (Only) so the tasmiyah is not sunnah between the Fatiha and the surah, and there is no dislike in it if it is done accidentally for the surah, whether he recites the surah aloud or silently. Wrong is the one who said that one should not say tasmiyah except in the first rak'ah. Then he recited the Fatiha and said amin secretly, its reality being to make oneself hear as before. Then he recited a surah from the mufassal as before, or recited three short verses or one long verse necessarily. Then every person praying says takbir for ruku', beginning the takbir at the start of bending and ending it at the end, to commence tasbih, so that no state of prayer is free from dhikr. He should be at ease, level his head with his back, take his knees with his hands, and the man should spread his fingers, stretch his legs, and bending like a bow is disliked. The woman does not spread her fingers. And glorify in it, i.e., the ruku', every person praying says 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Adhim' three times, and that number is the minimum of the recommended perfection. It is disliked to recite the Quran in ruku' and sujud and tashahhud by consensus of the Imams, because he said: 'I was forbidden to recite while bowing and prostrating.' Then he raised his head and stood at ease saying 'Sami'a Allahu li man hamidah' meaning Allah accepted from him who praised Him. Some scholars of apparent meaning, al-Nakha'i, and Ibn Sirin say he says it after recitation because Allah mentioned it with the letter fa, indicating immediate sequence, but this is not correct because the fa is for the present state. The commentary says: He also says thana during his following, though his imam preceded him with it, as long as he has not recited. It is said he says thana in his pauses, which is better. The words imply that the masbuq says thana twice, contrary to the well-known view. He does not come with ta'awwudh in ruku'. He comes with the takbirs of the two Eids in ruku'. The apparent reason indicates that there is no difference between the first and second rak'ah. The pronoun is singular considering the mentioned. The best in wudu is to say the basmala in the manner previously mentioned, and in dhabiha to say 'Bismillah Allahu Akbar'. The restriction to surah indicates dislike if he does it for verses. The prohibition of reciting Quran in ruku' and sujud and tashahhud: as for the supplications in tashahhud that contain words of the Quran, one should intend supplication, not recitation, otherwise it is prohibitively disliked.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement discussing rulings on ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, takbir for ruku', and the prohibition of Quran recital in bowing and prostrating. The ta'awwudh is recited secretly (sirran) before the Fatiha. The masbuq (latecomer) recites ta'awwudh at the start of what he makes up after the thana (opening supplication). However, he does not recite it in ruku'. The ta'awwudh is delayed after the extra takbirs in Eid prayer. The tasmiyah (basmala) is said before the Fatiha in every rak'ah, whether fard or nafl. It is not sunnah between Fatiha and surah, but if accidentally done for the surah, it's not disliked. The muqtadi does not say tasmiyah because he does not recite. Imam Abu Yusuf differed, considering it a follower of thana. Then the Fatiha and amin are recited secretly. After Fatiha, a surah from the mufassal or three short verses is recited. Then the takbir for ruku' is performed, starting with the bowing action. The person prays in ruku' says 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Adhim' three times, considered the minimum perfection. It is disliked (makruh) to recite Quran in ruku', sujud, and tashahhud by consensus, based on the hadith 'I was forbidden to recite while bowing or prostrating.' The text also discusses the wording of 'Sami'a Allahu li man hamidah' and a minor dispute about its timing. The masbuq says thana (opening supplication) while following the imam, and some say he says it twice, though the well-known view is once. The commentary ends with a note on supplications using Quranic words in tashahhud.

Key Terms
التعوذ (al-ta'awwudh): Seeking refuge in Allah from Shaytan by saying 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim'.
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): Saying 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' before reciting the Fatiha in prayer.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A person who joins the prayer late after the imam has already started.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Ta'awwudh and tasmiyah are sunnah acts recited secretly before the Fatiha; the muqtadi does not recite them; reciting Quran in ruku' is makruh due to the explicit prohibition in the hadith.

Rulings on Ta'awwudh and Basmalah for Masbuq and General Prayer
Explains rulings of ta'awwudh and basmalah, with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on ta'awwudh for the masbuq and muqtadi, explain the intra-madhhab dispute with Abu Yusuf, and apply the ruling on basmalah between Fatihah and surah.

Core Idea
The masbuq recites ta'awwudh silently at the start of each missed rak'ah; the muqtadi does not recite at all.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah on Maraqi al-Falah refines the rulings on ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) and tasmiyah (basmalah) in prayer. It clarifies when and how the latecomer (masbuq) recites ta'awwudh, addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute with Abu Yusuf regarding the follower (muqtadi), and provides guidance on the basmalah's placement between al-Fatihah and a surah. Understanding these details prevents common errors in prayer execution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on ta'awwudh for the masbuq
Locate where the passage states when the masbuq recites ta'awwudh: at the beginning of what he makes up after the thana', silently, and not in ruku'.
The masbuq recites ta'awwudh only once per missed rak'ah, at the start of his qiyam.
2
Analyze the dispute over the muqtadi's ta'awwudh
Note the difference between the matn's position (muqtadi does not recite) and Abu Yusuf's view (muqtadi is a follower of thana'). Understand the Hanafi response based on the purpose of ta'awwudh being for recitation, which the muqtadi does not perform.
The mufta bihi is the matn's position, rejecting Abu Yusuf's reasoning.
3
Examine the basmalah rulings
The passage states that the basmalah is recited silently before al-Fatihah in every rak'ah. It also clarifies that basmalah between al-Fatihah and the surah is not sunnah, but if done intentionally for the surah, there is no dislike.
This distinguishes Hanafi practice from other schools that consider basmalah obligatory between Fatihah and surah.
4
Understand the critique of the fa' argument
Some early scholars argue that ta'awwudh should be after recitation because the verse uses the letter fa (interpreted as succession). The passage refutes this by explaining that fa here indicates simultaneity (hal), not sequence.
This is a critical refinement of the proof, strengthening the Hanafi position.
5
Summarize the mufta bihi positions
Consolidate: masbuq recites ta'awwudh in the beginning of each missed rak'ah (after thana', before basmalah) and does not recite it in ruku'; muqtadi does not recite ta'awwudh; basmalah is sunnah before Fatihah in every rak'ah, and it is not sunnah between Fatihah and surah, but no dislike if done for the surah.
These rulings are the operative positions for fatwa.
